<div class="NavHead" style="font-size: 105%; background: transparent; text-align: left;">Ethnic groups</div>
<ul class="NavContent" style="list-style: none none; margin-left: 0; text-align:left; display:none; font-size: 105%; margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: inherit;"><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0">0.4% <a href="/wiki/British_Mixed" class="mw-redirect" title="British Mixed">White &amp; Other</a></li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0">&#160;</li><li style="line-height: inherit; </div></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Demonym" title="Demonym">Demonym(s)</a></th><td>Sheffielder</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Time_zone" title="Time zone">Time zone</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/UTC%2B0" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC+0">UTC+0</a> (<a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Mean_Time" title="Greenwich Mean Time">Greenwich Mean Time</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Postcode</th><td class="adr"><div class="postal-code"><a href="/wiki/S_postcode_area" title="S postcode area">S</a></div></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbering_plan" title="Telephone numbering plan">Area code(s)</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/0114_(UK_dial_code)" class="mw-redirect" title="0114 (UK dial code)">0114</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Website</th><td><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.sheffield.gov.uk">www.sheffield.gov.uk</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Sheffield</b> is a <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city</a> and <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_borough" title="Metropolitan borough">metropolitan borough</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Yorkshire" title="South Yorkshire">South Yorkshire</a>, England. <a href="/wiki/Historic_counties_of_England" title="Historic counties of England">Historically</a> part of the <a href="/wiki/West_Riding_of_Yorkshire" title="West Riding of Yorkshire">West Riding of Yorkshire</a>, its name derives from the <a href="/wiki/River_Sheaf" title="River Sheaf">River Sheaf</a>, which runs through the city. With some of its southern suburbs annexed from <a href="/wiki/Derbyshire" title="Derbyshire">Derbyshire</a>, the city has grown from its largely industrial roots to encompass a wider economic base. The population of the City of Sheffield is 582,506 (mid-2018&#160;est.)<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and it is one of the eight largest regional English cities that make up the <a href="/wiki/Core_Cities_Group" title="Core Cities Group">Core Cities Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Sheffield is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_districts_by_population" title="List of English districts by population">third-largest</a> English district by population. The metropolitan population of Sheffield is 1,569,000.<sup id="cite_ref-espon.eu_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-espon.eu-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The city is in the eastern foothills of the <a href="/wiki/Pennines" title="Pennines">Pennines</a>, and the valleys of the <a href="/wiki/River_Don,_Yorkshire" title="River Don, Yorkshire">River Don</a> and its four tributaries, the <a href="/wiki/River_Loxley" title="River Loxley">Loxley</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Porter_Brook" title="Porter Brook">Porter Brook</a>, the <a href="/wiki/River_Rivelin" title="River Rivelin">Rivelin</a> and the <a href="/wiki/River_Sheaf" title="River Sheaf">Sheaf</a>. Sixty-one per cent of Sheffield's entire area is green space, and a third of the city lies within the <a href="/wiki/Peak_District" title="Peak District">Peak District</a> <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">national park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sheffgeog_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheffgeog-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> There are more than 250 parks, woodlands and gardens in the city,<sup id="cite_ref-sheffgeog_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheffgeog-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> which is estimated to contain around 4.5 million trees.<sup id="cite_ref-GEO_treecount_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GEO_treecount-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sheffield played a crucial role in the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, with many significant inventions and technologies developed in the city. In the 19th&#160;century, the city saw a huge expansion of its traditional cutlery trade, when <a href="/wiki/Stainless_steel" title="Stainless steel">stainless steel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crucible_steel" title="Crucible steel">crucible steel</a> were developed locally, fuelling an almost tenfold increase in the population. Sheffield received its <a href="/wiki/Municipal_charter" title="Municipal charter">municipal charter</a> in 1843, becoming the City of Sheffield in 1893. International competition in iron and steel caused a decline in these industries in the 1970s and 1980s, coinciding with the collapse of coal mining in the area.
</p><p>The 21st&#160;century has seen extensive <a href="/wiki/Urban_renewal" title="Urban renewal">redevelopment</a> in Sheffield, along with other British cities.  Sheffield's <a href="/wiki/Gross_value_added" title="Gross value added">gross value added</a> (GVA) has increased by 60% since 1997, standing at £9.2&#160;billion in 2007. The economy has experienced steady growth averaging around 5% annually, greater than that of the broader region of <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_and_the_Humber" title="Yorkshire and the Humber">Yorkshire and the Humber</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The city has a long sporting heritage, and is home to the world's oldest football club, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_F.C." title="Sheffield F.C.">Sheffield F.C.</a><sup id="cite_ref-celebration_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-celebration-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Games between the two professional clubs, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_F.C." title="Sheffield United F.C.">Sheffield United</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wednesday_F.C." title="Sheffield Wednesday F.C.">Sheffield Wednesday</a>, are known as the <a href="/wiki/Steel_City_derby" title="Steel City derby">Steel City derby</a>. The city is also home to the <a href="/wiki/World_Snooker_Championship" title="World Snooker Championship">World Snooker Championship</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Steelers" title="Sheffield Steelers">Sheffield Steelers</a>, the UK's first professional ice hockey team.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Sheffield" title="History of Sheffield">History of Sheffield</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ruins_of_Sheffield_Manor_1819_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Lithograph drawing showing a large stately home in ruins" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Ruins_of_Sheffield_Manor_1819_1.jpg/220px-Ruins_of_Sheffield_Manor_1819_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Ruins_of_Sheffield_Manor_1819_1.jpg/330px-Ruins_of_Sheffield_Manor_1819_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Ruins_of_Sheffield_Manor_1819_1.jpg/440px-Ruins_of_Sheffield_Manor_1819_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2012" data-file-height="1401" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ruins_of_Sheffield_Manor_1819_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Manor" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield Manor">Sheffield Manor</a> ruins as they appeared <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;1819</span></div></div></div>
<p>The area now occupied by the City of Sheffield is believed to have been inhabited since at least the late <a href="/wiki/Upper_Paleolithic" title="Upper Paleolithic">Upper Paleolithic</a>, about 12,800 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The earliest evidence of human occupation in the Sheffield area was found at <a href="/wiki/Creswell_Crags" title="Creswell Crags">Creswell Crags</a> to the east of the city. In the <a href="/wiki/British_Iron_Age" title="British Iron Age">Iron Age</a> the area became the southernmost territory of the <a href="/wiki/Pennines" title="Pennines">Pennine</a> tribe called the <a href="/wiki/Brigantes" title="Brigantes">Brigantes</a>. It is this tribe who are thought to have constructed several hill forts in and around Sheffield.<sup id="cite_ref-VICKERS_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VICKERS-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the departure of the Romans, the Sheffield area may have been the southern part of the <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Britons" title="Celtic Britons">Brittonic</a> kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Elmet" title="Elmet">Elmet</a>, with the rivers Sheaf and Don forming part of the boundary between this kingdom and the kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Mercia" title="Mercia">Mercia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Gradually, <a href="/wiki/Angles" title="Angles">Anglian</a> settlers pushed west from the kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Deira" title="Deira">Deira</a>. A Britonnic presence within the Sheffield area is evidenced by two settlements called <a href="/wiki/Wales,_South_Yorkshire" title="Wales, South Yorkshire">Wales</a> and Waleswood close to Sheffield.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The settlements that grew and merged to form Sheffield, however, date from the second half of the first millennium, and are of <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Anglo-Saxon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Danelaw" title="Danelaw">Danish</a> origin.<sup id="cite_ref-VICKERS_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VICKERS-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In Anglo-Saxon times, the Sheffield area straddled the border between the kingdoms of <a href="/wiki/Mercia" title="Mercia">Mercia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Northumbria" title="Kingdom of Northumbria">Northumbria</a>. The <i><a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon_Chronicle" title="Anglo-Saxon Chronicle">Anglo-Saxon Chronicle</a></i> reports that <a href="/wiki/Eanred_of_Northumbria" title="Eanred of Northumbria">Eanred of Northumbria</a> submitted to <a href="/wiki/Egbert_of_Wessex" class="mw-redirect" title="Egbert of Wessex">Egbert of Wessex</a> at the hamlet of <a href="/wiki/Dore" title="Dore">Dore</a> (now a suburb of Sheffield) in 829,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> a key event in the unification of the kingdom of England under the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Wessex" title="House of Wessex">House of Wessex</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Norman_conquest_of_England" title="Norman conquest of England">Norman conquest of England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Castle" title="Sheffield Castle">Sheffield Castle</a> was built to protect the local settlements, and a small town developed that is the nucleus of the modern city.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> By 1296, a market had been established at what is now known as <a href="/wiki/Castle_Square,_Sheffield" title="Castle Square, Sheffield">Castle Square</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and Sheffield subsequently grew into a small <a href="/wiki/Market_town" title="Market town">market town</a>.  In the 14th&#160;century, Sheffield was already noted for the production of <a href="/wiki/Knife" title="Knife">knives</a>, as mentioned in <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Chaucer" title="Geoffrey Chaucer">Geoffrey Chaucer</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Canterbury_Tales" title="The Canterbury Tales">The Canterbury Tales</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and by the early 1600s it had become the main centre of <a href="/wiki/Cutlery" title="Cutlery">cutlery</a> manufacture in England outside London, overseen by the <a href="/wiki/Company_of_Cutlers_in_Hallamshire" title="Company of Cutlers in Hallamshire">Company of Cutlers in Hallamshire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> From 1570 to 1584, <a href="/wiki/Mary,_Queen_of_Scots" title="Mary, Queen of Scots">Mary, Queen of Scots</a>, was imprisoned in Sheffield Castle and <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Manor" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield Manor">Sheffield Manor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dale_dike_reservoir.jpg" class="image"><img alt="View across a partially wooded valley containing a reservoir" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Dale_dike_reservoir.jpg/220px-Dale_dike_reservoir.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Dale_dike_reservoir.jpg/330px-Dale_dike_reservoir.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Dale_dike_reservoir.jpg/440px-Dale_dike_reservoir.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dale_dike_reservoir.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dale_Dike_Reservoir" title="Dale Dike Reservoir">Dale Dike Reservoir</a>: the original dam wall of this reservoir collapsed in 1864 causing the <a href="/wiki/Great_Sheffield_Flood" title="Great Sheffield Flood">Great Sheffield Flood</a></div></div></div>
<p>During the 1740s, a form of the <a href="/wiki/Crucible_steel" title="Crucible steel">crucible steel</a> process was discovered that allowed the manufacture of a better quality of steel than had previously been possible.<sup id="cite_ref-Tweedale1986_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tweedale1986-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In about the same period, a technique was developed for fusing a thin sheet of silver onto a copper ingot to produce silver plating, which became widely known as <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_plate" title="Sheffield plate">Sheffield plate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> These innovations spurred Sheffield's growth as an industrial town,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> but the loss of some important export markets led to a recession in the late 18th and early 19th&#160;century. The resulting poor conditions culminated in a <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a> epidemic that killed 402&#160;people in 1832.<sup id="cite_ref-VICKERS_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VICKERS-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The population of the town grew rapidly throughout the 19th&#160;century; increasing from 60,095 in 1801 to 451,195 by 1901.<sup id="cite_ref-VICKERS_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VICKERS-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_and_Rotherham_Railway" title="Sheffield and Rotherham Railway">Sheffield and Rotherham railway</a> was constructed in 1838, connecting the two towns. The town was incorporated as a <a href="/wiki/Borough" title="Borough">borough</a> in 1842, and was granted a <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city charter</a> in 1893.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The influx of people also led to demand for better water supplies, and a number of new reservoirs were constructed on the outskirts of the town.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Women_of_steel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photo of the statue Women of Steel at barker&#39;s Pool, Sheffield" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Women_of_steel.jpg/170px-Women_of_steel.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Women_of_steel.jpg/255px-Women_of_steel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Women_of_steel.jpg/340px-Women_of_steel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1993" data-file-height="2905" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Women_of_steel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <i><a href="/wiki/Women_of_Steel" title="Women of Steel">Women of Steel</a></i> statue commemorates the women of Sheffield who worked in the city's steel industry during the First and Second World Wars</div></div></div>
<p>The collapse of the dam wall of one of these reservoirs in 1864 resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Sheffield_Flood" title="Great Sheffield Flood">Great Sheffield Flood</a>, which killed 270 people and devastated large parts of the town.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The growing population led to the construction of many back-to-back dwellings that, along with severe pollution from the factories, inspired <a href="/wiki/George_Orwell" title="George Orwell">George Orwell</a> in 1937 to write: "Sheffield, I suppose, could justly claim to be called the ugliest town in the <a href="/wiki/Old_World" title="Old World">Old World</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">The Great Depression</a> hit the city in the 1930s, but as international tensions increased and the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> became imminent; Sheffield's steel factories were set to work manufacturing weapons and ammunition for the war effort. As a result, the city became a target for bombing raids, the heaviest of which occurred on the nights of 12 and 15 December 1940, now known as the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Blitz" title="Sheffield Blitz">Sheffield Blitz</a>. The city was protected by barrage balloons managed from RAF Norton <sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> More than 660&#160;lives were lost and many buildings destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Parkhill2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Panorama of a brutalist housing estate" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Parkhill2.jpg/220px-Parkhill2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Parkhill2.jpg/330px-Parkhill2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Parkhill2.jpg/440px-Parkhill2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="333" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Parkhill2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Park_Hill,_Sheffield" title="Park Hill, Sheffield">Park Hill flats</a>, an example of 1950s and 1960s council housing estates in Sheffield</div></div></div>
<p>In the 1950s and 1960s, many of the city's slums were demolished, and replaced with housing schemes such as the <a href="/wiki/Park_Hill,_Sheffield" title="Park Hill, Sheffield">Park Hill flats</a>. Large parts of the city centre were also cleared to make way for a new system of roads.<sup id="cite_ref-VICKERS_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VICKERS-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Increased automation and competition from abroad resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Steel_crisis" title="Steel crisis">closure of many steel mills</a>. The 1980s saw the worst of this run-down of Sheffield's industries, along with those of many other areas of the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The building of the <a href="/wiki/Meadowhall_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Meadowhall Centre">Meadowhall Centre</a> on the site of a former steelworks in 1990 was a mixed blessing, creating much-needed jobs but hastening the decline of the city centre. Attempts to regenerate the city were kick-started when the city hosted the 1991 <a href="/wiki/Universiade" title="Universiade">World Student Games</a>, which saw the construction of new sporting facilities such as the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Arena" title="Sheffield Arena">Sheffield Arena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Don_Valley_Stadium" title="Don Valley Stadium">Don Valley Stadium</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ponds_Forge" title="Ponds Forge">Ponds Forge</a> complex.<sup id="cite_ref-VICKERS_9-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VICKERS-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sheffield is changing rapidly as new projects regenerate some of the more run-down parts of the city. One such, the <i>Heart of the City Project</i>, has initiated a number of public works in the city centre: the <a href="/wiki/Peace_Gardens" title="Peace Gardens">Peace Gardens</a> were renovated in 1998, the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Galleries" class="mw-redirect" title="Millennium Galleries">Millennium Galleries</a> opened in April 2001, the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Winter_Gardens" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield Winter Gardens">Winter Gardens</a> were opened in May 2003, and a public space to link these two areas, the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Square_(Sheffield)" class="mw-redirect" title="Millennium Square (Sheffield)">Millennium Square</a>, was opened in May 2006. Additional developments included the remodelling of <a href="/wiki/Sheaf_Square" title="Sheaf Square">Sheaf Square</a>, in front of the refurbished railway station. The square contains "The Cutting Edge", a sculpture designed by Si Applied Ltd<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> and made from Sheffield steel.
</p><p>Sheffield was particularly hard hit during the <a href="/wiki/2007_United_Kingdom_floods" title="2007 United Kingdom floods">2007 United Kingdom floods</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Winter_of_2009-2010_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Winter of 2009-2010 in the United Kingdom">2010 'Big Freeze'</a>. Many landmark buildings such as Meadowhall and the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wednesday" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield Wednesday">Sheffield Wednesday</a> ground flooded due to being close to rivers that flow through the city. In 2010, 5,000 properties in Sheffield were identified as still being at risk of flooding. In 2012 the city narrowly escaped another flood, despite extensive work by the Environment Agency to clear local river channels since the 2007 event. In 2014 Sheffield Council's cabinet approved plans to further reduce the possibility of flooding by adopting plans to increase water catchment on tributaries of the River Don.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2012, there have been disputes between the city council and residents over the fate of the city's 36,000 highway trees, with 4,000 having been felled as part of a scheme to maintain the city streets.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> However, there have been plans for the highway maintenance to replant all felled trees across the city, including those historically felled and not previously replanted.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_local_elections" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield local elections">Sheffield local elections</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PeaceGdnsSheffd.jpg" class="image"><img alt="View across a garden containing people enjoying a sunny day towards a large Victorian building with a clock tower" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/PeaceGdnsSheffd.jpg/300px-PeaceGdnsSheffd.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/PeaceGdnsSheffd.jpg/450px-PeaceGdnsSheffd.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/PeaceGdnsSheffd.jpg/600px-PeaceGdnsSheffd.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PeaceGdnsSheffd.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Town_Hall" title="Sheffield Town Hall">Sheffield Town Hall</a>, adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/Peace_Gardens" title="Peace Gardens">Peace Gardens</a>, is an example of <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian era</a> <a href="/wiki/Gothic_revival_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Gothic revival architecture">Gothic revival architecture</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Sheffield is governed at the local level by <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_City_Council" title="Sheffield City Council">Sheffield City Council</a>. It consists of 84&#160;councillors elected to represent 28&#160;<a href="/wiki/Ward_(politics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ward (politics)">wards</a>: three councillors per ward. Following the 2016 local elections, the distribution of council seats is <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> 56, <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> 20, the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales" title="Green Party of England and Wales">Green Party</a> 4 and <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Independence_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Independence Party">UKIP</a> 4. The city also has a <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor_of_Sheffield" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Mayor of Sheffield">Lord Mayor</a>; though now simply a ceremonial position, in the past the office carried considerable authority, with executive powers over the finances and affairs of the city council.
</p><p>For much of its history the council was controlled by the Labour Party, and was noted for its <a href="/wiki/Left-wing_politics" title="Left-wing politics">leftist</a> sympathies; during the 1980s, when Sheffield City Council was led by <a href="/wiki/David_Blunkett" title="David Blunkett">David Blunkett</a>, the area gained the epithet the "<a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_South_Yorkshire" title="People&#39;s Republic of South Yorkshire">Socialist Republic of South Yorkshire</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> However, the Liberal Democrats controlled the Council between 1999 and 2001 and took control again from 2008 to 2011.
</p><p>The majority of council-owned facilities are operated by independent charitable trusts. <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_International_Venues" title="Sheffield International Venues">Sheffield International Venues</a> runs many of the city's sporting and leisure facilities, including <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Arena" title="Sheffield Arena">Sheffield Arena</a> and the <a href="/wiki/English_Institute_of_Sport_%E2%80%93_Sheffield" class="mw-redirect" title="English Institute of Sport – Sheffield">English Institute of Sport</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Galleries_and_Museums_Trust" title="Sheffield Galleries and Museums Trust">Museums Sheffield</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Industrial_Museums_Trust" title="Sheffield Industrial Museums Trust">Sheffield Industrial Museums Trust</a> take care of galleries and museums owned by the council.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The city returns five members of parliament to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a>, with a sixth, the Member of Parliament for <a href="/wiki/Penistone_and_Stocksbridge_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Penistone and Stocksbridge (UK Parliament constituency)">Penistone and Stocksbridge</a> representing parts of Sheffield and Barnsley.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The former Deputy Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Nick_Clegg" title="Nick Clegg">Nick Clegg</a> was an MP for Sheffield, representing <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Hallam_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Sheffield Hallam (UK Parliament constituency)">Sheffield Hallam</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Sheffield" title="Geography of Sheffield">Geography of Sheffield</a></div>
<p>Sheffield is located at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Sheffield&amp;params=53_23_N_1_28_W_type:city_region:GB"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">53°23′N</span> <span class="longitude">1°28′W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">53.383°N 1.467°W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">53.383; -1.467</span></span></span></a></span>. It lies directly beside <a href="/wiki/Rotherham" title="Rotherham">Rotherham</a>, from which it is separated largely by the <a href="/wiki/M1_motorway" title="M1 motorway">M1 motorway</a>. Although <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Borough_of_Barnsley" title="Metropolitan Borough of Barnsley">Barnsley Metropolitan Borough</a> also borders Sheffield to the north, the town itself is a few miles further away. The southern and western borders of the city are shared with <a href="/wiki/Derbyshire" title="Derbyshire">Derbyshire</a>; in the first half of the 20th&#160;century Sheffield extended its borders south into Derbyshire, annexing a number of villages,<sup id="cite_ref-derbyshire_expansion_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-derbyshire_expansion-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/Totley" title="Totley">Totley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dore" title="Dore">Dore</a> and the area now known as <a href="/wiki/Mosborough" class="mw-redirect" title="Mosborough">Mosborough</a> Townships. Directly to the west of the city are the <a href="/wiki/Peak_District" title="Peak District">Peak District National Park</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pennines" title="Pennines">Pennine</a> upland range, while the lowlands of the <a href="/wiki/South_Yorkshire_Coalfield" title="South Yorkshire Coalfield">South Yorkshire Coalfield</a> lie to the east.
</p><p>Sheffield is a geographically diverse city.<sup id="cite_ref-GEO_diverse_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GEO_diverse-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Lying in the eastern foothills of the Pennines,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> the city nestles in a natural amphitheatre created by several hills<sup id="cite_ref-number_of_hills_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-number_of_hills-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> and the confluence of five rivers: <a href="/wiki/River_Don,_South_Yorkshire" class="mw-redirect" title="River Don, South Yorkshire">Don</a>, <a href="/wiki/River_Sheaf" title="River Sheaf">Sheaf</a>, <a href="/wiki/River_Rivelin" title="River Rivelin">Rivelin</a>, <a href="/wiki/River_Loxley" title="River Loxley">Loxley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Porter_Brook" title="Porter Brook">Porter</a>. As such, much of the city is built on hillsides with views into the city centre or out to the countryside. Blake Street, in the S6 postcode area, is the third steepest residential street in England, with a gradient of 16.6°.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The city's lowest point is just 29 metres (95&#160;ft) above sea level near <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Meadows" title="Blackburn Meadows">Blackburn Meadows</a>, while some parts of the city are at over 500 metres (1,640&#160;ft); the highest point being 548 metres (1,798&#160;ft) at <a href="/wiki/High_Stones" title="High Stones">High Stones</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Margery_Hill" title="Margery Hill">Margery Hill</a>. However, 79% of the housing in the city is between 100 and 200 metres (330 and 660&#160;ft) above sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Estimated to contain around 4.5 million trees,<sup id="cite_ref-GEO_treecount_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GEO_treecount-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Sheffield has more trees per person than any other city in Europe, and it is claimed by Sheffield City Council to be England's greenest city,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> a claim that was reinforced when it won the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Entente_Florale" title="Entente Florale">Entente Florale</a> competition. With more than 250 parks, woodlands and gardens, it has over 170&#160;woodlands (covering 10.91&#160;sq&#160;mi or 28.3&#160;km<sup>2</sup>), 78&#160;public parks (covering 7.07&#160;sq&#160;mi or 18.3&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) and 10&#160;public gardens. Added to the 52.0 square miles (134.7&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) of national park and 4.20 square miles (10.9&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) of water this means that 61% of the city is <a href="/wiki/Open_space_reserve" title="Open space reserve">greenspace</a>. Despite this, about 64% of Sheffield householders live further than 300 metres (328&#160;yd) from their nearest greenspace, although access is better in less affluent neighbourhoods across the city.<sup id="cite_ref-sheffgeog_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheffgeog-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Sheffield also has a very wide variety of <a href="/wiki/Habitat" title="Habitat">habitat</a>, comparing favourably with any city in the United Kingdom: urban, parkland and woodland, agricultural and arable land, moors, meadows and freshwater-based habitats. There are six areas within the city that are designated as <a href="/wiki/List_of_Sites_of_Special_Scientific_Interest_in_South_Yorkshire" title="List of Sites of Special Scientific Interest in South Yorkshire">sites of special scientific interest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The present city boundaries were set in 1974 (with slight modification in 1994), when the former <a href="/wiki/County_borough" title="County borough">county borough</a> of Sheffield merged with <a href="/wiki/Stocksbridge" title="Stocksbridge">Stocksbridge</a> <a href="/wiki/Urban_district_(Great_Britain_and_Ireland)" title="Urban district (Great Britain and Ireland)">Urban District</a> and two parishes from the <a href="/wiki/Wortley_Rural_District" title="Wortley Rural District">Wortley Rural District</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sheffgeog_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheffgeog-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> This area includes a significant part of the countryside surrounding the main urban region. Roughly a third of Sheffield lies in the <a href="/wiki/Peak_District" title="Peak District">Peak District National Park</a>. No other English city had parts of a national park within its boundary,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> until the creation in March 2010 of the <a href="/wiki/South_Downs_National_Park" title="South Downs National Park">South Downs National Park</a>, part of which lies within <a href="/wiki/Brighton_and_Hove" title="Brighton and Hove">Brighton and Hove</a>.
</p>
<div role="navigation" class="navbox" aria-labelledby="Neighbouring_towns_and_cities" style="padding:3px"><table class="nowraplinks mw-collapsible autocollapse navbox-inner" style="border-spacing:0;background:transparent;color:inherit"><tbody><tr><th scope="col" class="navbox-title" colspan="2"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Adjacent_communities" title="Template:Adjacent communities"><abbr title="View this template" style=";;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none; padding:0;">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Adjacent_communities" title="Template talk:Adjacent communities"><abbr title="Discuss this template" style=";;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none; padding:0;">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Adjacent_communities&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template" style=";;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none; padding:0;">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div><div id="Neighbouring_towns_and_cities" style="font-size:114%;margin:0 4em">Neighbouring towns and cities</div></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0px"><div style="padding:0em 0.25em"><table role="presentation" style="width:100%; margin:0; text-align:center;"><tbody><tr>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Like the rest of the United Kingdom, the climate in Sheffield is generally <a href="/wiki/Temperate" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperate">temperate</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Pennines" title="Pennines">Pennines</a> to the west of the city can create a cool, gloomy and wet environment, but they also provide shelter from the prevailing westerly winds, casting a "rain shadow" across the area.<sup id="cite_ref-Met_NE_England_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Met_NE_England-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Between 1971 and 2000 Sheffield averaged 824.7 millimetres (32.47&#160;in) of rain per year; December was the wettest month with 91.9 millimetres (3.62&#160;in) and July the driest with 51.0 millimetres (2.01&#160;in). July was also the hottest month, with an average maximum temperature of 20.8&#160;°C (69.4&#160;°F). The highest temperature ever recorded in the city of Sheffield was 35.6&#160;°C (96.1&#160;°F), on 25 July 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The average minimum temperature in January and February was 1.6&#160;°C (34.9&#160;°F),<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> though the lowest temperatures recorded in these months can be between −10 and −15&#160;°C (14 and 5&#160;°F), although since 1960, the temperature has never fallen below −9.2&#160;°C (15.4&#160;°F),<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> suggesting that urbanisation around the Weston Park site during the second half of the 20th&#160;century may prevent temperatures below −10&#160;°C (14&#160;°F) occurring.
</p><p>The coldest temperature to be recorded in recent years was −8.2&#160;°C (17.2&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> (Note: The official Weston Park Weather Station statistics, which can also be viewed at <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Central_Library" title="Sheffield Central Library">Sheffield Central Library</a>, has the temperature at −8.7&#160;°C (16.3&#160;°F), recorded on 20 December, and states that to be the lowest December temperature since 1981.) The coldest temperature ever recorded in the city of Sheffield at <a href="/wiki/Weston_Park,_Sheffield" title="Weston Park, Sheffield">Weston Park</a>, since records began in 1882, is −14.6&#160;°C (5.7&#160;°F), registered in February 1895.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The lowest daytime maximum temperature in the city since records began is −5.6&#160;°C (21.9&#160;°F), also recorded in February 1895.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> More recently, a −4.4&#160;°C (24.1&#160;°F) was recorded as a daytime maximum at Weston Park, on 20 December 2010.(from the Weston Park Weather Station statistics, which also can be viewed at Sheffield Central Library.) On average, through the winter months of December to March, there are 67 days during which ground frost occurs.<sup id="cite_ref-Met_NE_England_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Met_NE_England-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<tr>
<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center;font-size:95%;">Source #1: <a href="/wiki/Met_Office" title="Met Office">Met Office</a><sup id="cite_ref-Met_Averages_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Met_Averages-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center;font-size:95%;">Source #2: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Meteorological_Institute" title="Royal Netherlands Meteorological Institute">KNMI</a><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and WeatherAtlas<sup id="cite_ref-Weather-Atlas_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weather-Atlas-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
</div>
<p><br />
The Weston Park Weather station, established in 1882, is one of the longest running weather stations in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>. It has recorded weather for more than 125 years, and a 2008 report showed that the climate of Sheffield is warming faster than it has at any time during this period, with 1990 and 2006 being the hottest years on record.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In collaboration with the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Environment_Institute" title="Stockholm Environment Institute">Stockholm Environment Institute</a>, Sheffield developed a <a href="/wiki/Carbon_footprint" title="Carbon footprint">carbon footprint</a> (based on 2004/05 consumption figures) of 5,798,361&#160;<a href="/wiki/Tonnes" class="mw-redirect" title="Tonnes">tonnes</a> per year. This compares to the UK's total carbon footprint of 698,568,010&#160;tonnes per year. The factors with the greatest impact are housing (34%), transport (25%), consumer (11%), private services (9%), public services (8%), food (8%) and capital investment (5%).<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Sheffield City Council has signed up to the <a href="/wiki/10:10" title="10:10">10:10</a> campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-planet_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-planet-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_belt">Green belt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Green belt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/South_and_West_Yorkshire_Green_Belt" title="South and West Yorkshire Green Belt">South and West Yorkshire Green Belt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Sheffield" title="Geography of Sheffield">Geography of Sheffield</a></div>
<p>Sheffield is within a <a href="/wiki/Green_belt_(United_Kingdom)" title="Green belt (United Kingdom)">green belt</a> region that extends into the wider surrounding counties, and is in place to reduce <a href="/wiki/Urban_sprawl" title="Urban sprawl">urban sprawl</a>, prevent the towns and areas in the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_urban_area" title="Sheffield urban area">Sheffield built-up area</a> conurbation from further convergence, protect the identity of outlying communities, encourage <a href="/wiki/Brownfield" class="mw-redirect" title="Brownfield">brownfield</a> reuse, and preserve nearby countryside. This is achieved by restricting inappropriate development within the designated areas, and imposing stricter conditions on permitted building.<sup id="cite_ref-belt1_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-belt1-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-belt2_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-belt2-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The main urban area and larger villages of the borough are exempt from the green belt area, but surrounding smaller villages, hamlets and rural areas are 'washed over' with the designation. A subsidiary aim of the green belt is to encourage recreation and leisure interests,<sup id="cite_ref-belt1_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-belt1-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> with many rural landscape features and facilities included.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subdivisions">Subdivisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Subdivisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Areas_of_Sheffield" title="Areas of Sheffield">Areas of Sheffield</a></div>
<p>Sheffield is made up of many suburbs and neighbourhoods, many of which developed from villages or <a href="/wiki/Hamlet_(place)" title="Hamlet (place)">hamlets</a> that were absorbed into Sheffield as the city grew.<sup id="cite_ref-VICKERS_9-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VICKERS-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> These historical areas are largely ignored by the modern administrative and political divisions of the city; instead it is divided into 28&#160;electoral <a href="/wiki/Ward_(politics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ward (politics)">wards</a>, with each ward generally covering 4–6&#160;areas.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> These electoral wards are grouped into six <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_constituencies" title="United Kingdom constituencies">parliamentary constituencies</a>. Sheffield is largely <a href="/wiki/Civil_parishes_in_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil parishes in England">unparished</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Bradfield,_South_Yorkshire" title="Bradfield, South Yorkshire">Bradfield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ecclesfield" title="Ecclesfield">Ecclesfield</a> have parish councils, and <a href="/wiki/Stocksbridge" title="Stocksbridge">Stocksbridge</a> has a town council.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Skyline">Skyline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Skyline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin:0 auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1008px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_wide_from_Meersbrook_Park.jpg" class="image" title="Panorama of Sheffield taken from Meersbrook Park"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Sheffield_wide_from_Meersbrook_Park.jpg/1000px-Sheffield_wide_from_Meersbrook_Park.jpg" decoding="async" width="1000" height="191" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Sheffield_wide_from_Meersbrook_Park.jpg/1500px-Sheffield_wide_from_Meersbrook_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Sheffield_wide_from_Meersbrook_Park.jpg/2000px-Sheffield_wide_from_Meersbrook_Park.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6992" data-file-height="1332" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_wide_from_Meersbrook_Park.jpg" title="File:Sheffield wide from Meersbrook Park.jpg"> </a></div>Panorama of Sheffield taken from <a href="/wiki/Meersbrook_Park" title="Meersbrook Park">Meersbrook Park</a></div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_Sheffield" title="Demography of Sheffield">Demography of Sheffield</a></div><table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 0.5em;"><tbody><tr><th class="navbox-title" colspan="3" style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1971 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">572,794</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">−0.4%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1981 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">530,844</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">−7.3%</td></tr><tr><th solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left"><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2001" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2001">United Kingdom Census 2001</a> reported a resident population for Sheffield of 513,234, a 2% decline from the 1991 census.<sup id="cite_ref-Sheffield_2001_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sheffield_2001-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The city is part of the wider <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_urban_area" title="Sheffield urban area">Sheffield urban area</a>, which had a population of 640,720.<sup id="cite_ref-SUA_2001_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SUA_2001-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2011">In 2011</a> the racial composition of Sheffield's population was 84% <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">White</a> (81% <a href="/wiki/White_British" title="White British">White British</a>, 0.5% <a href="/wiki/Irish_migration_to_Great_Britain" title="Irish migration to Great Britain">White Irish</a>, 0.1% <a href="/wiki/Gypsy_(term)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gypsy (term)">Gypsy</a> or <a href="/wiki/Irish_Traveller" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Traveller">Irish Traveller</a>, 2.3% <a href="/wiki/Other_White" title="Other White">Other White</a>), 2.4% of <a href="/wiki/Mixed_(United_Kingdom_ethnicity_category)" title="Mixed (United Kingdom ethnicity category)">mixed race</a> (1.0% White and Black Caribbean, 0.2% White and Black African, 0.6% White and Asian, 0.6% Other Mixed), 8% <a href="/wiki/British_Asian" title="British Asian">Asian</a> (1.1% <a href="/wiki/British_Indian" title="British Indian">Indian</a>, 4% <a href="/wiki/British_Pakistanis" title="British Pakistanis">Pakistani</a>, 0.6% <a href="/wiki/British_Bangladeshi" title="British Bangladeshi">Bangladeshi</a>, 1.3% <a href="/wiki/British_Chinese" title="British Chinese">Chinese</a>, 1.0% Other Asian), 3.6% <a href="/wiki/Black_British" title="Black British">Black</a> (2.1% African, 1% <a href="/wiki/British_African-Caribbean_people" title="British African-Caribbean people">Caribbean</a>, 0.5% <a href="/wiki/Other_Black" class="mw-redirect" title="Other Black">Other Black</a>), 1.5% <a href="/wiki/British_Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="British Arab">Arab</a> and 0.7% of other ethnic heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="citation gives National Identity not Ethnicity (February 2018)">failed verification</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In terms of religion, 53% of the population are Christian, 6% are Muslim, 0.6% are Hindu, 0.4% are Buddhist, 0.2% are Sikh, 0.1% are Jewish, 0.4% belong to another religion, 31% have no religion and 7% did not state their religion.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The largest <a href="/wiki/Quinary" title="Quinary">quinary</a> group is 20- to 24-year-olds (9%) because of the large university student population.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The population of Sheffield peaked in 1951 at 577,050, and has since declined steadily. However, the mid-2007 population estimate was 530,300, representing an increase of about 17,000 residents since 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although a city, Sheffield is informally known as "the <a href="/wiki/Largest_village_in_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Largest village in England">largest village in England</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-BaldwinBottomsWalker_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BaldwinBottomsWalker-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Binfield_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Binfield-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BurgoyneClark_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BurgoyneClark-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> because of a combination of topographical isolation and demographic stability.<sup id="cite_ref-BaldwinBottomsWalker_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BaldwinBottomsWalker-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> It is relatively geographically isolated, being cut off from other places by a ring of hills.<sup id="cite_ref-Hampton_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hampton-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TaylorEvansFraser_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TaylorEvansFraser-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Local folklore insists that, like Rome, Sheffield was built "on seven hills".<sup id="cite_ref-TaylorEvansFraser_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TaylorEvansFraser-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The land surrounding Sheffield was unsuitable for industrial use,<sup id="cite_ref-BaldwinBottomsWalker_72-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BaldwinBottomsWalker-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> and now includes several protected <a href="/wiki/Green_belt" title="Green belt">green belt</a> areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Mann_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mann-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> These topographical factors have served to restrict urban spread,<sup id="cite_ref-Mann_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mann-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> resulting in a relatively stable population size and a low degree of mobility.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Sheffield" title="Economy of Sheffield">Economy of Sheffield</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_in_Sheffield" title="List of companies in Sheffield">List of companies in Sheffield</a></div>

<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pauls_Place_Sheffield.png" class="image"><img alt="St Paul&#39;s Tower, a new, mixed use development which forms part of the St Paul&#39;s Place development. In the top left corner is the Main St Paul&#39;s tower itself. Below it is the Tower 2, connected to the main tower but half the height. To the right is another office building in the same development. All have been completed within the last 5 years and represent some of the newest architecture in the city." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/St_Pauls_Place_Sheffield.png/170px-St_Pauls_Place_Sheffield.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/St_Pauls_Place_Sheffield.png/255px-St_Pauls_Place_Sheffield.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/St_Pauls_Place_Sheffield.png/340px-St_Pauls_Place_Sheffield.png 2x" data-file-width="493" data-file-height="658" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pauls_Place_Sheffield.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Place" title="St Paul&#39;s Place">St Paul's Place</a>, 2010. <a href="/wiki/St_Pauls_Tower" class="mw-redirect" title="St Pauls Tower">St Paul's Tower</a>, the tallest building in Sheffield, is in the centre.</div></div></div><p>After many years of decline, the Sheffield economy is going through a strong revival. The 2004 <a href="/wiki/Barclays_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Barclays Bank">Barclays Bank</a> Financial Planning study<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> revealed that, in 2003, the Sheffield district of <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Hallam_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Sheffield Hallam (UK Parliament constituency)">Hallam</a> was the highest ranking area outside London for overall wealth, the proportion of people earning over £60,000 a year standing at almost 12%. A survey by <a href="/wiki/Knight_Frank" title="Knight Frank">Knight Frank</a><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> revealed that Sheffield was the fastest-growing city outside London for office and residential space and rents during the second half of 2004. This can be seen in a surge of redevelopments, including the <a href="/wiki/St_Pauls_Tower" class="mw-redirect" title="St Pauls Tower">City Lofts Tower</a> and accompanying <a href="/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Place" title="St Paul&#39;s Place">St Paul's Place</a>, <a href="/wiki/Velocity_Living" class="mw-redirect" title="Velocity Living">Velocity Living</a> and the Moor redevelopment,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> the forthcoming <a href="/wiki/New_Retail_Quarter" class="mw-redirect" title="New Retail Quarter">NRQ</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Winter_Gardens" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield Winter Gardens">Winter Gardens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peace_Gardens" title="Peace Gardens">Peace Gardens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Galleries" class="mw-redirect" title="Millennium Galleries">Millennium Galleries</a> and many projects completed under the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_One" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield One">Sheffield One</a> redevelopment agency. The Sheffield economy grew from £5.6&#160;billion in 1997 (1997 GVA)<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> to £9.2&#160;billion in 2007 (2007 GVA).<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The "UK Cities Monitor 2008" placed Sheffield among the top ten "best cities to locate a business today", the city occupying third and fourth places respectively for best office location and best new <a href="/wiki/Call_centre" title="Call centre">call centre</a> location. The same report places Sheffield in third place regarding "greenest reputation" and second in terms of the availability of financial incentives.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bessemer_5180.JPG" class="image"><img alt="The Bessemer Converter located at Kelham Island Museum. The converter is located within an old industrial facility typical of those constructed during the Industrial Revolution." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Bessemer_5180.JPG/220px-Bessemer_5180.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Bessemer_5180.JPG/330px-Bessemer_5180.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Bessemer_5180.JPG/440px-Bessemer_5180.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bessemer_5180.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sir <a href="/wiki/Henry_Bessemer" title="Henry Bessemer">Henry Bessemer</a>’s <a href="/wiki/Bessemer_converter" class="mw-redirect" title="Bessemer converter">Bessemer converter</a>, the most important technique for making <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a> from the 1850s to the 1950s, located at <a href="/wiki/Kelham_Island_Museum" title="Kelham Island Museum">Kelham Island Museum</a>, Sheffield</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harry_Brearley.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Harry_Brearley.jpg/220px-Harry_Brearley.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Harry_Brearley.jpg/330px-Harry_Brearley.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Harry_Brearley.jpg/440px-Harry_Brearley.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="479" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harry_Brearley.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Monument to <a href="/wiki/Harry_Brearley" title="Harry Brearley">Harry Brearley</a> and the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Stainless_steel" title="Stainless steel">stainless steel</a> at the former <a href="/wiki/Firth_Brown_Steels" title="Firth Brown Steels">Brown Firth Research Laboratories</a></div></div></div>
<p>Sheffield has an international reputation for metallurgy and steel-making.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Playing a crucial role in the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, the city became an industrial powerhouse in the 18th century, and was dubbed "<a href="/wiki/Steel_City" title="Steel City">Steel City</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Steel_BBC_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steel_BBC-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Many innovations in these fields have been made in Sheffield, for example <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Huntsman" title="Benjamin Huntsman">Benjamin Huntsman</a> discovered the <a href="/wiki/Crucible_technique" class="mw-redirect" title="Crucible technique">crucible technique</a> in the 1740s at his workshop in <a href="/wiki/Handsworth,_South_Yorkshire" title="Handsworth, South Yorkshire">Handsworth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> This process was rendered obsolete in 1856 by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Bessemer" title="Henry Bessemer">Henry Bessemer</a>'s invention of the <a href="/wiki/Bessemer_converter" class="mw-redirect" title="Bessemer converter">Bessemer converter</a>. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Boulsover" title="Thomas Boulsover">Thomas Boulsover</a> invented <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Plate" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield Plate">Sheffield Plate</a> (silver-plated copper) in the early 18th&#160;century. 
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Stainless_steel" title="Stainless steel">Stainless steel</a> was invented by <a href="/wiki/Harry_Brearley" title="Harry Brearley">Harry Brearley</a> in 1912, bringing affordable <a href="/wiki/Cutlery" title="Cutlery">cutlery</a> to the masses.<sup id="cite_ref-Steel_BBC_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steel_BBC-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> The work of <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Brian_Pickering" title="Frederick Brian Pickering">F. B. Pickering</a> and T. Gladman throughout the 1960s, 1970s and 1980s was fundamental to the development of modern high-strength low-alloy steels.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Further innovations continue, with new advanced manufacturing technologies and techniques being developed on the <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Manufacturing_Park" title="Advanced Manufacturing Park">Advanced Manufacturing Park</a> by Sheffield's universities and other independent research organisations.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Organisations located on the AMP include the Advanced Manufacturing Research Centre (AMRC, a research partnership between the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing Company">Boeing Company</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sheffield" title="University of Sheffield">University of Sheffield</a>), Castings Technology International (CTI), <a href="/wiki/The_Welding_Institute" title="The Welding Institute">The Welding Institute</a> (TWI),<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="Rolls-Royce plc">Rolls-Royce plc</a> and <a href="/wiki/McLaren_Automotive" title="McLaren Automotive">McLaren Automotive</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Forgemasters" title="Sheffield Forgemasters">Forgemasters</a>, founded in 1805, is the sole remaining independent <a href="/wiki/Steel_works" class="mw-redirect" title="Steel works">steel works</a> in the world and dominates the north east of Sheffield around the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Don_Valley" title="Lower Don Valley">Lower Don Valley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The firm has a global reputation for producing the largest and most complex steel forgings and castings and is certified to produce critical nuclear components, with recent projects including the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Astute_class_submarine" class="mw-redirect" title="Astute class submarine"><i>Astute</i>-class</a> submarines.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The firm also has the capacity for pouring the largest single ingot (570 tonnes) in Europe and is currently in the process of expanding its capabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While iron and steel have long been the main industries of Sheffield, <a href="/wiki/Coal_mining" title="Coal mining">coal mining</a> has also been a major industry, particularly in the outlying areas, and the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Westminster" title="Palace of Westminster">Palace of Westminster</a> in London was built using <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> from <a href="/wiki/Quarry" title="Quarry">quarries</a> in the nearby village of <a href="/wiki/Anston" title="Anston">Anston</a>. Other areas of employment include <a href="/wiki/Call_centre" title="Call centre">call centres</a>, the <a href="/wiki/City_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="City Council">City Council</a>, universities and hospitals.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fargate_sheffield_2.png" class="image"><img alt="Fargate shopping precinct, Sheffield. Once a busy road, it has been pedestrianised for several decades and is Sheffield&#39;s main City Centre shopping area, home to many well-known companies. The image shows classical architecture on both sides with one plan spaces in the centre, dotted with trees and the buildings on the High Street are visible beyond the trees." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Fargate_sheffield_2.png/220px-Fargate_sheffield_2.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Fargate_sheffield_2.png/330px-Fargate_sheffield_2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Fargate_sheffield_2.png/440px-Fargate_sheffield_2.png 2x" data-file-width="870" data-file-height="658" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fargate_sheffield_2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fargate shopping area</div></div></div>
<p>Sheffield is a major retail centre, and is home to many <a href="/wiki/High_Street" title="High Street">High Street</a> and <a href="/wiki/Department_store" title="Department store">department stores</a> as well as designer boutiques.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The main shopping areas in the city centre are on <a href="/wiki/The_Moor_Quarter" title="The Moor Quarter">The Moor</a> precinct, <a href="/wiki/Fargate" title="Fargate">Fargate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orchard_Square" title="Orchard Square">Orchard Square</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Devonshire_Quarter" title="Devonshire Quarter">Devonshire Quarter</a>. Department stores in the city centre include <a href="/wiki/John_Lewis_Partnership" title="John Lewis Partnership">John Lewis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marks_and_Spencer" class="mw-redirect" title="Marks and Spencer">Marks and Spencer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atkinsons" title="Atkinsons">Atkinsons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Debenhams" title="Debenhams">Debenhams</a>. Sheffield's main market was once <a href="/wiki/Castle_Market" title="Castle Market">Castle Market</a>, built above the remains of the castle. This has since been demolished.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Moor_Quarter#Moor_Market" title="The Moor Quarter">Sheffield Moor Market</a> opened in 2013. Shopping areas outside the city centre include the <a href="/wiki/Meadowhall_Shopping_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Meadowhall Shopping Centre">Meadowhall</a> shopping centre and retail parks, <a href="/wiki/Ecclesall_Road" title="Ecclesall Road">Ecclesall Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Road_(Sheffield)" title="London Road (Sheffield)">London Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hillsborough,_South_Yorkshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Hillsborough, South Yorkshire">Hillsborough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Firth_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Firth Park">Firth Park</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Peaks" title="Crystal Peaks">Crystal Peaks</a> shopping centre. In a 2010 survey of forecast expenditure at retail centres in the United Kingdom, Meadowhall was ranked 12th and <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_City_Centre" title="Sheffield City Centre">Sheffield City Centre</a> 19th.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Three_Tuns,_Sheffield,_Aug._2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/The_Three_Tuns%2C_Sheffield%2C_Aug._2018.jpg/220px-The_Three_Tuns%2C_Sheffield%2C_Aug._2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/The_Three_Tuns%2C_Sheffield%2C_Aug._2018.jpg/330px-The_Three_Tuns%2C_Sheffield%2C_Aug._2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/The_Three_Tuns%2C_Sheffield%2C_Aug._2018.jpg/440px-The_Three_Tuns%2C_Sheffield%2C_Aug._2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1040" data-file-height="780" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Three_Tuns,_Sheffield,_Aug._2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Three Tuns, Sheffield, the iconic triangular, corner architectural delight, and former Nun's washhouse, circa early 1800s</div></div></div>
<p>Sheffield has a District Energy system that exploits the city's domestic waste, by <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Incinerator" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield Incinerator">incinerating</a> it and converting the energy from it to electricity. It also provides hot water, which is distributed through over 25 miles (40&#160;km) of pipes under the city, via two networks. These networks supply heat and hot water for many buildings throughout the city. These include not only cinemas, hospitals, shops and offices, but also universities (<a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Hallam_University" title="Sheffield Hallam University">Sheffield Hallam University</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sheffield" title="University of Sheffield">University of Sheffield</a>), and residential properties.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Energy generated in a waste plant produces 60&#160;<a href="/wiki/Megawatt" class="mw-redirect" title="Megawatt">megawatts</a> of thermal energy and up to 19&#160;<a href="/wiki/Megawatt" class="mw-redirect" title="Megawatt">megawatts</a> of electrical energy from 225,000&#160;<a href="/wiki/Tonnes" class="mw-redirect" title="Tonnes">tonnes</a> of waste.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_City_Region_Enterprise_Zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield City Region Enterprise Zone">Sheffield City Region Enterprise Zone</a> was launched to promote development in a number of sites in Sheffield and across the wider region. In March 2014 additional sites were added to the zone.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Sheffield" title="Transport in Sheffield">Transport in Sheffield</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_and_international_travel">National and international travel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: National and international travel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Station_from_Sheaf_Square.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Night view across an open plaza dominated by a long curving water feature that is decoratively lit. At the far side of the plaza there is the arched frontage of a railway station building" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Sheffield_Station_from_Sheaf_Square.jpg/220px-Sheffield_Station_from_Sheaf_Square.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Sheffield_Station_from_Sheaf_Square.jpg/330px-Sheffield_Station_from_Sheaf_Square.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Sheffield_Station_from_Sheaf_Square.jpg/440px-Sheffield_Station_from_Sheaf_Square.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Station_from_Sheaf_Square.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sheffield_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield railway station">Sheffield railway station</a></div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Sheffield is linked into the national motorway network via the <a href="/wiki/M1_motorway" title="M1 motorway">M1</a> and <a href="/wiki/M18_motorway_(Great_Britain)" title="M18 motorway (Great Britain)">M18</a> motorways.<sup id="cite_ref-OS_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OS-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> The M1 skirts the north-east of the city, linking Sheffield with London to the south and <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a> to the north, and crosses <a href="/wiki/Tinsley_Viaduct" title="Tinsley Viaduct">Tinsley Viaduct</a> near Rotherham; the M18 branches from the M1 close to Sheffield, linking the city with <a href="/wiki/Doncaster" title="Doncaster">Doncaster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_Sheffield_Airport" title="Doncaster Sheffield Airport">Doncaster Sheffield Airport</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Humber" title="Humber">Humber</a> ports. The <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Parkway" title="Sheffield Parkway">Sheffield Parkway</a> connects the city centre with the motorways.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
