<p>Major railway routes through <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield railway station">Sheffield railway station</a> include the <a href="/wiki/Midland_Main_Line" title="Midland Main Line">Midland Main Line</a>, which links the city to London via the East Midlands, the <a href="/wiki/Cross_Country_Route" title="Cross Country Route">Cross Country Route</a> which links the East of Scotland and Northeast of England with the <a href="/wiki/West_Midlands_(region)" title="West Midlands (region)">West Midlands</a> and the Southwest, and the lines linking Liverpool and Manchester with <a href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Hull" title="Kingston upon Hull">Hull</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Anglia" title="East Anglia">East Anglia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> With the redevelopment of London St Pancras station (now <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_International" class="mw-redirect" title="St Pancras International">St Pancras International</a>) complete, Sheffield has a direct connection to <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">continental Europe</a>. <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Railway" title="East Midlands Railway">East Midlands Railway</a> run services to St Pancras International and <a href="/wiki/Eurostar" title="Eurostar">Eurostar</a> run services from there to France and Belgium.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Master_Cutler_(train)" title="Master Cutler (train)">Master Cutler</a></i>, a named passenger express train running from Sheffield railway station to London St Pancras, provides a direct connection to the capital.
</p><p>It is planned that <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_2" title="High Speed 2">High Speed 2</a> will serve a city centre station in Sheffield, via a spur from the main HS2 line. It is scheduled to be operational by 2033 with services to Birmingham, London, Leeds and Newcastle. There will be four trains an hour serving the station, with journey times to London and Birmingham reduced to 1 hour 19 minutes and 48 minutes respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other trains serving Sheffield (apart from East Midland Trains) are provided by <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a>, <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a>. Aside from the main railway station there are five other stations in Sheffield. <a href="/wiki/Meadowhall_Interchange" title="Meadowhall Interchange">Meadowhall</a>, a bus, rail and tram interchange, is the second largest station and accommodates a number of services including the long distance <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a> service. <a href="/wiki/Dore_and_Totley_railway_station" title="Dore and Totley railway station">Dore and Totley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Woodhouse_railway_station" title="Woodhouse railway station">Woodhouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chapeltown_railway_station" title="Chapeltown railway station">Chapeltown</a> and <a href="/wiki/Darnall_railway_station" title="Darnall railway station">Darnall</a> stations serve as <a href="/wiki/Commuter_rail_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Commuter rail in the United Kingdom">commuter stations</a> for suburban communities but are also connected to the <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Great_Britain" title="Rail transport in Great Britain">national rail network</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Train_station,_Shefield.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Train_station%2C_Shefield.jpg/220px-Train_station%2C_Shefield.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Train_station%2C_Shefield.jpg/330px-Train_station%2C_Shefield.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Train_station%2C_Shefield.jpg/440px-Train_station%2C_Shefield.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2046" data-file-height="1535" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Train_station,_Shefield.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sheffield railway station, 2013</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Coach">Coach</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Coach">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Coach_(vehicle)" class="mw-redirect" title="Coach (vehicle)">Coach</a> services running through Sheffield are operated by <a href="/wiki/National_Express_Coaches" title="National Express Coaches">National Express</a> and to a lesser extent <a href="/wiki/Megabus_(Europe)" title="Megabus (Europe)">Megabus</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_Group" title="Stagecoach Group">Stagecoach Group</a>. National Express services call at <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Interchange" title="Sheffield Interchange">Sheffield Interchange</a>, Meadowhall Interchange and Meadowhead Bus Stop. Megabus services only call at Meadowhall. National Express services 564, 560, 350, 320, 310 and 240 call at Sheffield, as do others on a less frequent basis.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The 560/564 service is a direct connection to London <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Coach_Station" title="Victoria Coach Station">Victoria Coach Station</a> via <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield_coach_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Chesterfield coach station">Chesterfield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Coachway" title="Milton Keynes Coachway">Milton Keynes</a>, operating 12 times a day in both directions. The 350 and 240 services connect Sheffield to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow</a>/<a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick</a> Airports respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Two Megabus services, the M12 and M20, call at Sheffield en route to London from <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle upon Tyne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Inverness" title="Inverness">Inverness</a> respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Canal">Canal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Canal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_and_South_Yorkshire_Navigation" title="Sheffield and South Yorkshire Navigation">Sheffield and South Yorkshire Navigation</a> (S&amp;SY) is a system of navigable inland waterways (<a href="/wiki/Canal" title="Canal">canals</a> and canalised rivers) in Yorkshire and <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire" title="Lincolnshire">Lincolnshire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Chiefly based on the <a href="/wiki/River_Don,_South_Yorkshire" class="mw-redirect" title="River Don, South Yorkshire">River Don</a>, it runs for a length of 43 miles (69&#160;km) and has 29&#160;<a href="/wiki/Canal_lock" class="mw-redirect" title="Canal lock">locks</a>. It connects Sheffield, <a href="/wiki/Rotherham" title="Rotherham">Rotherham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doncaster" title="Doncaster">Doncaster</a> with the <a href="/wiki/River_Trent" title="River Trent">River Trent</a> at <a href="/wiki/Keadby" title="Keadby">Keadby</a> and (via the <a href="/wiki/New_Junction_Canal" title="New Junction Canal">New Junction Canal</a>) the <a href="/wiki/Aire_and_Calder_Navigation" title="Aire and Calder Navigation">Aire and Calder Navigation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Following the closure of <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_City_Airport" title="Sheffield City Airport">Sheffield City Airport</a> in 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> the closest international airport to Sheffield is <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_Sheffield_Airport" title="Doncaster Sheffield Airport">Doncaster Sheffield Airport</a> which is located 18 miles (29&#160;km) from the city centre. It operates on the site of the former <a href="/wiki/RAF_Finningley" title="RAF Finningley">RAF Finningley</a>. It opened on 28 April 2005 and is served mainly by charter and budget airlines. It handles about one million passengers a year.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A link road, opened in February 2016, connects Doncaster Sheffield Airport to the M18 motorway, reducing the journey time from Sheffield city centre from 40 to 25 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Airport" title="East Midlands Airport">East Midlands Airport</a> is within one hour's drive of the city, and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester Airport</a> is connected directly to Sheffield by <a href="/wiki/South_TransPennine" class="mw-redirect" title="South TransPennine">a direct train</a> every hour.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_travel">Local travel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Local travel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Parkway.png" class="image"><img alt="The start of the Sheffield Parkway, as viewed from Park Square, where it meets the City Centre. The road, in the centre, is six lanes wide and leads towards the Parkway Edge development (left-centre) where the road meets the Inner Ring Road. To the right is the Sheffield Supertram viaduct and beyond that a new apartment complex." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Sheffield_Parkway.png/220px-Sheffield_Parkway.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Sheffield_Parkway.png/330px-Sheffield_Parkway.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Sheffield_Parkway.png/440px-Sheffield_Parkway.png 2x" data-file-width="876" data-file-height="658" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Parkway.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Parkway" title="Sheffield Parkway">Sheffield Parkway</a> terminus at <a href="/wiki/Park_Square,_Sheffield" title="Park Square, Sheffield">Park Square</a>. The opposite end connects to the <a href="/wiki/M1_motorway" title="M1 motorway">M1 motorway</a> at Junction 33.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/A57_road" title="A57 road">A57</a> and <a href="/wiki/A61_road" title="A61 road">A61 roads</a> are the major <a href="/wiki/Trunk_road" title="Trunk road">trunk roads</a> through Sheffield.<sup id="cite_ref-OS_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OS-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> These run east–west and north–south respectively, crossing in the city centre, from where the other major roads generally radiate spoke-like. An inner <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Inner_Ring_Road" title="Sheffield Inner Ring Road">ring road</a>, mostly constructed in the 1970s and extended in 2007 to form a complete ring,<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> allows traffic to avoid the city centre, and an <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Outer_Ring_Road" title="Sheffield Outer Ring Road">outer ring road</a> runs to the east, south east and north, nearer the edge of the city, but does not serve the western side of Sheffield.<sup id="cite_ref-OS_100-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OS-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sheffield does not have as extensive a suburban and inter-urban railway network as other comparable British cities.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> However, there are several local rail routes running along the city's valleys and beyond, connecting it with other parts of <a href="/wiki/South_Yorkshire" title="South Yorkshire">South Yorkshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire" title="West Yorkshire">West Yorkshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nottinghamshire" title="Nottinghamshire">Nottinghamshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire" title="Lincolnshire">Lincolnshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Derbyshire" title="Derbyshire">Derbyshire</a>. These local routes include the <a href="/wiki/Penistone_Line" title="Penistone Line">Penistone Line</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dearne_Valley_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Dearne Valley Line">Dearne Valley Line</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hope_Valley_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Hope Valley Line">Hope Valley Line</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Hallam_Line" title="Hallam Line">Hallam Line</a>. As well as the main stations of <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Midland_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield Midland station">Sheffield</a> and Meadowhall, there are five suburban stations, at <a href="/wiki/Chapeltown_railway_station" title="Chapeltown railway station">Chapeltown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darnall_railway_station" title="Darnall railway station">Darnall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Woodhouse_railway_station" title="Woodhouse railway station">Woodhouse</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dore_%26_Totley_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Dore &amp; Totley railway station">Dore &amp; Totley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Interchange_2.png" class="image"><img alt="Sheffield Interchange, the main hub for bus and coach operations in Sheffield. In the foreground is the interchange itself. Visible in the bottom left corner is the new, main entrance to the interchange. In the centre are the long bus stands that form the interchange. Above that is the Digital Campus commercial development built upon an unused section of the interchange. In the top left corner is the 1960s Park Hill flats development and to the right is Sheffield Railway Station." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Sheffield_Interchange_2.png/220px-Sheffield_Interchange_2.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Sheffield_Interchange_2.png/330px-Sheffield_Interchange_2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Sheffield_Interchange_2.png/440px-Sheffield_Interchange_2.png 2x" data-file-width="871" data-file-height="583" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Interchange_2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Interchange" title="Sheffield Interchange">Sheffield Interchange</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Supertram" title="Sheffield Supertram">Sheffield Supertram</a> (not derived from the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Tramway" title="Sheffield Tramway">previous tramways</a>), operated by <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_Group" title="Stagecoach Group">Stagecoach</a>, opened in 1994, shortly after the similar <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Metrolink" title="Manchester Metrolink">Metrolink</a> scheme in Manchester. Its network consists of 37 miles (60&#160;km) of track and four lines, from Halfway to <a href="/wiki/Malin_Bridge" title="Malin Bridge">Malin Bridge</a> (Blue Line), from Meadowhall to <a href="/wiki/Middlewood,_South_Yorkshire" title="Middlewood, South Yorkshire">Middlewood</a> (Yellow Line), from Meadowhall to <a href="/wiki/Herdings_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Herdings Park">Herdings Park</a> (Purple Line),<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> and the tram-train line from <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Cathedral" title="Sheffield Cathedral">Cathedral</a> to <a href="/wiki/Rotherham_Parkgate" class="mw-redirect" title="Rotherham Parkgate">Rotherham Parkgate</a> (Black Line), with all four lines running via the city centre. The network operated as three lines for years before it was extended to Rotherham Parkgate in 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> with a fleet of new "train-trams" sharing a conventional rail line between Sheffield and Rotherham. The system contains both on-street and segregated running, depending upon the section and line.
</p><p>
The Supertram serves as an important connection between areas in the North East of Sheffield (namely Meadowhall and <a href="/wiki/Valley_Centertainment" title="Valley Centertainment">Valley Centertainment</a>) and the city centre. Because it is operated by the <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_Group" title="Stagecoach Group">Stagecoach Group</a>, the ticketing system for the Supertram is integrated with Stagecoach buses in Sheffield, meaning passengers can switch between the two modes of transport without having to buy a separate ticket.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Sheffield's local bus infrastructure has its main hub at <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Interchange" title="Sheffield Interchange">Sheffield Interchange</a>. Other bus stations lie at <a href="/wiki/Halfway,_Sheffield" class="mw-redirect" title="Halfway, Sheffield">Halfway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hillsborough,_South_Yorkshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Hillsborough, South Yorkshire">Hillsborough</a> and <a href="/wiki/Darnall#Meadowhall" title="Darnall">Meadowhall</a>. A flurry of new operators was created after deregulation in 1986,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> though a series of mergers has reduced the number. </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Supertram_2010.png" class="image"><img alt="A Sheffield Supertram in current blue, orange and red Stagecoach livery. The Tram shown is cross the Park Square junction. Behind it is the bridge connecting the junction and tracks to Sheffield city centre. The whole square (now 20 years since redevelopment) is covered in trees and plants and new buildings can be seen beyond them." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Sheffield_Supertram_2010.png/220px-Sheffield_Supertram_2010.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Sheffield_Supertram_2010.png/330px-Sheffield_Supertram_2010.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Sheffield_Supertram_2010.png/440px-Sheffield_Supertram_2010.png 2x" data-file-width="835" data-file-height="616" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Supertram_2010.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Sheffield Supertram</div></div></div>
<p>There are numerous bus operators within Sheffield: <a href="/wiki/First_South_Yorkshire" title="First South Yorkshire">First South Yorkshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_Yorkshire" title="Stagecoach Yorkshire">Stagecoach Yorkshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/TM_Travel" title="TM Travel">TM Travel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hulleys_of_Baslow" title="Hulleys of Baslow">Hulleys of Baslow</a>, Powells, G&amp;J Holmes and <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Community_Transport" title="Sheffield Community Transport">Sheffield Community Transport</a>. First South Yorkshire, became by far the largest bus operator and in recent years implemented a series of fare rises and service cuts which saw bus ridership drop.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Recent developments have seen <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_Sheffield" title="Stagecoach Sheffield">Stagecoach Sheffield</a> taking over <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Terrier_(bus_company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Yorkshire Terrier (bus company)">Yorkshire Terrier</a>, Andrews and parent company <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Traction" title="Yorkshire Traction">Yorkshire Traction</a>, thus forming one company and in the process expanding their bus services in the city. This has resulted in increased competition, and price drops on certain routes.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Zero-fare" class="mw-redirect" title="Zero-fare">zero-fare</a> bus service, the <i>FreeBee</i> (Operated by <a href="/wiki/First_South_Yorkshire" title="First South Yorkshire">First South Yorkshire</a>), operated a circular route around the city centre from the Sheffield Interchange. The FreeBee buses stopped in 2014 and is due to save £8 million.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There is also the <a href="/wiki/Bus_Rapid_Transit_North" title="Bus Rapid Transit North">Bus Rapid Transit North</a> route between Sheffield and <a href="/wiki/Maltby,_South_Yorkshire" title="Maltby, South Yorkshire">Maltby</a> via Rotherham. In 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Bus_Rapid_Transit" class="mw-redirect" title="Bus Rapid Transit">Bus Rapid Transit</a> scheme was approved by the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_and_Humber_Assembly" title="Yorkshire and Humber Assembly">Yorkshire and Humber Assembly</a>'s Regional Transport Board and there were plans for two routes; one (the Northern route) to Rotherham via Meadowhall and <a href="/wiki/Templeborough" title="Templeborough">Templeborough</a>, and the other via the developing employment centre and Waverley.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> The route between Sheffield and Maltby was approved in 2013 with construction commencing in January 2014, involving the construction of the new 800m Tinsley Road Link between Meadowhall and the A6178 road.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> The route opened in September 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cycling">Cycling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Cycling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>For cycling, although hilly, Sheffield is compact and has few major trunk roads. It is on the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Pennine_Trail" class="mw-redirect" title="Trans-Pennine Trail">Trans-Pennine Trail</a>, a <a href="/wiki/National_Cycle_Network" title="National Cycle Network">National Cycle Network</a> route running from West to East from <a href="/wiki/Southport" title="Southport">Southport</a> in Merseyside to <a href="/wiki/Hornsea" title="Hornsea">Hornsea</a> in the <a href="/wiki/East_Riding_of_Yorkshire" title="East Riding of Yorkshire">East Riding of Yorkshire</a> and North to South from <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a> in West Yorkshire to <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield" title="Chesterfield">Chesterfield</a> in Derbyshire.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> There are many cycle routes going along country paths in the woods surrounding the city, though very few cycle lanes in the city itself.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Sheffield" title="Education in Sheffield">Education in Sheffield</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Arts_Tower.png" class="image"><img alt="Blue/Grey skyscraper with a glass curtain wall. In the foreground is park pond with a small wooden bridge and trees at either side. In between the Tower and the pond is a modern 2-storey building" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Sheffield_Arts_Tower.png/170px-Sheffield_Arts_Tower.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Sheffield_Arts_Tower.png/255px-Sheffield_Arts_Tower.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Sheffield_Arts_Tower.png/340px-Sheffield_Arts_Tower.png 2x" data-file-width="492" data-file-height="656" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Arts_Tower.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Arts_Tower" title="Arts Tower">Arts Tower</a>, on the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sheffield" title="University of Sheffield">University of Sheffield</a> campus</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SheffieldHallamNight.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/SheffieldHallamNight.jpg/220px-SheffieldHallamNight.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="66" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/SheffieldHallamNight.jpg/330px-SheffieldHallamNight.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/SheffieldHallamNight.jpg/440px-SheffieldHallamNight.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="1234" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SheffieldHallamNight.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hallam Square and the entrance to Sheffield Hallam University's City Campus</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Universities_and_colleges">Universities and colleges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Universities and colleges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sheffield has two universities, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sheffield" title="University of Sheffield">University of Sheffield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Hallam_University" title="Sheffield Hallam University">Sheffield Hallam University</a>. The two combined bring about 65,000&#160;students to the city every year.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (November 2017)">failed verification</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Sheffield University was established in 1897 as University College Sheffield and became the University of Sheffield in 1905.
</p><p>Sheffield Hallam University (SHU) is a university on two sites in Sheffield. City Campus is located in the city centre, close to Sheffield railway station, and <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_Crescent" title="Collegiate Crescent">Collegiate Crescent</a> Campus is about two miles away, adjacent to <a href="/wiki/Ecclesall_Road" title="Ecclesall Road">Ecclesall Road</a> in south-west Sheffield. The university is the third largest in the UK, with more than 37,000 students (of whom over 4,000 are international students), 4,170 staff and 747 courses. Sheffield Hallam University's history goes back to 1843 with the establishment of the Sheffield School of Design. During the 1960s several independent colleges (including the School of Design) joined to become Sheffield Polytechnic (Sheffield City Polytechnic from 1976) and was finally renamed Sheffield Hallam University in 1992.
</p><p>Sheffield has three main <a href="/wiki/Further_education" title="Further education">further education</a> providers: <a href="/wiki/The_Sheffield_College" title="The Sheffield College">The Sheffield College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Longley_Park_Sixth_Form_College" title="Longley Park Sixth Form College">Longley Park Sixth Form College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chapeltown_Academy" title="Chapeltown Academy">Chapeltown Academy</a>. <a href="/wiki/The_Sheffield_College" title="The Sheffield College">The Sheffield College</a> is organised on a federal basis and was originally created from the merger of six colleges around the city, since reduced to just four: Sheffield City (formerly Castle)<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> near the city centre, Hillsborough, serving the north of the city and Norton and Peaks to the south.
</p>
<h3><span id="Secondary.2C_primary_and_pre-school_education"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Secondary,_primary_and_pre-school_education">Secondary, primary and pre-school education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Secondary, primary and pre-school education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Sheffield" title="List of schools in Sheffield">List of schools in Sheffield</a></div>
<p>There are 137&#160;primary schools, 26&#160;secondary schools – of which 10 have <a href="/wiki/Sixth_form" title="Sixth form">sixth forms</a>: (<a href="/wiki/High_Storrs_School_(Sheffield)" class="mw-redirect" title="High Storrs School (Sheffield)">High Storrs</a>, <a href="/wiki/King_Ecgbert_School" title="King Ecgbert School">King Ecgberts</a>, <a href="/wiki/King_Edward_VII_School_(Sheffield)" class="mw-redirect" title="King Edward VII School (Sheffield)">King Edward VII</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silverdale_School_(Sheffield)" class="mw-redirect" title="Silverdale School (Sheffield)">Silverdale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meadowhead_School" title="Meadowhead School">Meadowhead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tapton_School" title="Tapton School">Tapton</a>, <a href="/wiki/UTC_Sheffield" title="UTC Sheffield">UTC Sheffield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_School_(Sheffield)" class="mw-redirect" title="Notre Dame School (Sheffield)">Notre Dame Catholic High</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bradfield_School" title="Bradfield School">Bradfield</a> and <a href="/wiki/All_Saints_Catholic_High_School,_Sheffield" title="All Saints Catholic High School, Sheffield">All Saints Catholic High</a><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>) – and a sixth-form college, <a href="/wiki/Longley_Park_Sixth_Form_College" title="Longley Park Sixth Form College">Longley Park Sixth Form College</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The city's five independent private schools include <a href="/wiki/Birkdale_School" title="Birkdale School">Birkdale School</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_High_School_(South_Yorkshire)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield High School (South Yorkshire)">Sheffield High School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> There are also 12 special schools and a number of Integrated Resource Units in mainstream schools which are, along with all other schools, managed by Sheffield City Council.<sup id="cite_ref-sheffield2010_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheffield2010-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> All schools are non-selective, mixed sex schools (apart from <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_High_School,_South_Yorkshire" title="Sheffield High School, South Yorkshire">Sheffield High School</a> which is an all-girls school).<sup id="cite_ref-sheffield2010_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheffield2010-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
The Early Years Education and Childcare Service of Sheffield City Council manages 32 nurseries and children's centres in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-sheffield2010_135-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheffield2010-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Sheffield" title="Sport in Sheffield">Sport in Sheffield</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BramallLaneKop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/BramallLaneKop.jpg/220px-BramallLaneKop.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/BramallLaneKop.jpg/330px-BramallLaneKop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/BramallLaneKop.jpg/440px-BramallLaneKop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BramallLaneKop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bramall_Lane" title="Bramall Lane">Bramall Lane</a>, the home of <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield United FC">Sheffield United</a>, is close to the city centre</div></div></div>
<p>Sheffield has a long sporting heritage. In 1857 a collective of <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricketers</a> formed the world's first-ever official <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> club, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield FC">Sheffield FC</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> and the world's second-ever, <a href="/wiki/Hallam_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Hallam FC">Hallam FC</a>, who also play at the <a href="/wiki/Sandygate_Road" class="mw-redirect" title="Sandygate Road">world's oldest football ground</a> in the suburb of <a href="/wiki/Crosspool" title="Crosspool">Crosspool</a>. Sheffield and Hallam are today Sheffield's two major non-league sides, although Sheffield now play just outside the city in nearby <a href="/wiki/Dronfield" title="Dronfield">Dronfield</a>, Derbyshire. Sheffield and Hallam contest what has become known as the Sheffield derby. By 1860 there were 15&#160;football clubs in Sheffield, with the first ever amateur league and cup competitions taking place in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hillsborough_Stadium_interior.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Hillsborough_Stadium_interior.jpg/220px-Hillsborough_Stadium_interior.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Hillsborough_Stadium_interior.jpg/330px-Hillsborough_Stadium_interior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Hillsborough_Stadium_interior.jpg/440px-Hillsborough_Stadium_interior.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="360" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hillsborough_Stadium_interior.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hillsborough_Stadium" title="Hillsborough Stadium">Hillsborough</a>, the home of <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wednesday_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield Wednesday FC">Sheffield Wednesday</a>, is the city's largest stadium with a capacity of just under 40,000</div></div></div><p> Sheffield is best known for its two professional football teams, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield United FC">Sheffield United</a>, known locally as The Blades, and <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wednesday_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield Wednesday FC">Sheffield Wednesday</a>, known locally as The Owls. United, who play at <a href="/wiki/Bramall_Lane" title="Bramall Lane">Bramall Lane</a> south of the city centre, compete in the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> and Wednesday, who play at <a href="/wiki/Hillsborough_Stadium" title="Hillsborough Stadium">Hillsborough</a> in the north west of the city, compete in the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Championship">Football League Championship</a>. The two clubs contest the <a href="/wiki/Steel_City_Derby" class="mw-redirect" title="Steel City Derby">Steel City Derby</a>, which is considered by many to be one of the most fierce football rivalries in English Football.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> In the pre-war era, both Wednesday and United enjoyed large amounts of success and found themselves two of the country's top clubs; Sheffield Wednesday have been champions of the Football League four times – in <a href="/wiki/1902%E2%80%9303_Football_League" title="1902–03 Football League">1902–03</a>, <a href="/wiki/1903-04_Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="1903-04 Football League">1903–04</a>, <a href="/wiki/1928-29_Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="1928-29 Football League">1928–29</a> and <a href="/wiki/1929-30_Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="1929-30 Football League">1929–30</a>, whilst Sheffield United have won it once, in <a href="/wiki/1897-98_Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="1897-98 Football League">1897–98</a>. During the 1970s and early 1980s the two sides fell from grace, with Wednesday finding themselves in the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">Third Division</a> by the mid 70s and United as far as the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Fourth_Division" title="Football League Fourth Division">Fourth Division</a> in <a href="/wiki/1980-81_in_English_football" class="mw-redirect" title="1980-81 in English football">1981</a>. Wednesday once again became one of England's high-flying clubs following promotion back to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">First Division</a> in <a href="/wiki/1983-84_in_English_football" class="mw-redirect" title="1983-84 in English football">1984</a>, winning the <a href="/wiki/1991_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="1991 Football League Cup Final">League Cup in 1991</a>, competing in the <a href="/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_UEFA_Cup" title="1992–93 UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup in 1992–93</a>, and reaching the final of both the <a href="/wiki/1993_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="1993 Football League Cup Final">League Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/1993_FA_Cup_Final" title="1993 FA Cup Final">FA Cup</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1992-93_in_English_football" class="mw-redirect" title="1992-93 in English football">same season</a>. United and Wednesday were both founding members of the <a href="/wiki/FA_Premier_League" class="mw-redirect" title="FA Premier League">Premier League</a> in 1992, but The Blades were relegated in <a href="/wiki/1993-94_in_English_football" class="mw-redirect" title="1993-94 in English football">1994</a>. The Owls remained until <a href="/wiki/1999-00_in_English_football" class="mw-redirect" title="1999-00 in English football">2000</a>. Both clubs have gone into decline in the 21st&#160;century, Wednesday twice relegated to <a href="/wiki/Football_League_One" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League One">League One</a> and United suffering the same fate in <a href="/wiki/2010-11_in_English_football" class="mw-redirect" title="2010-11 in English football">2011</a>, despite a brief spell in the Premier League in <a href="/wiki/2006-07_in_English_football" class="mw-redirect" title="2006-07 in English football">2006–07</a>. Sheffield Wednesday's new owner <a href="/wiki/Dejphon_Chansiri" title="Dejphon Chansiri">Dejphon Chansiri</a> is aiming for promotion back to the Premier League, which has currently resulted in two unsuccessful play-off campaigns but increased league standings.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PeleSheffield.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/PeleSheffield.jpg/170px-PeleSheffield.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/PeleSheffield.jpg/255px-PeleSheffield.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/PeleSheffield.jpg/340px-PeleSheffield.jpg 2x" data-file-width="864" data-file-height="1065" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PeleSheffield.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Brazilian legend <a href="/wiki/Pel%C3%A9" title="Pelé">Pelé</a> (left) in Sheffield in November 2007, marking the 150th anniversary of the world's oldest football club, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield FC">Sheffield FC</a><sup id="cite_ref-celebration_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-celebration-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div> 
<p>Sheffield was the site of the deadliest sports venue disaster in the United Kingdom, the <a href="/wiki/Hillsborough_disaster" title="Hillsborough disaster">Hillsborough disaster</a> in 1989, when 96 <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Liverpool FC">Liverpool</a> supporters were killed in a stampede and crush during an <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> semi final at the venue.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Rotherham_United_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Rotherham United FC">Rotherham United</a>, who play in League One, did play their home games in the city between 2008 and 2012, having moved to play at Sheffield's <a href="/wiki/Don_Valley_Stadium" title="Don Valley Stadium">Don Valley Stadium</a> in 2008 following a dispute with their previous landlord at their traditional home ground of <a href="/wiki/Millmoor" title="Millmoor">Millmoor</a>, Rotherham. However, in July 2012, the club moved to the new 12,000 seat <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stadium" title="New York Stadium">New York Stadium</a> in Rotherham. There are also facilities for golf, <a href="/wiki/Climbing" title="Climbing">climbing</a> and bowling, as well as a newly inaugurated national ice-skating arena (<a href="/wiki/IceSheffield" title="IceSheffield">IceSheffield</a>).
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Eagles" title="Sheffield Eagles">Sheffield Eagles</a> RLFC are the city's professional <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> team who play their matches at <a href="/wiki/Owlerton_Stadium" title="Owlerton Stadium">Owlerton Stadium</a>. They currently play in the second tier of the professional league, the <a href="/wiki/Co-operative_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Co-operative Championship">Championship</a> and are current champions, having won back to back titles in 2012 and 2013. Their most successful moment came in 1998, when, against all the odds they defeated <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Warriors" title="Wigan Warriors">Wigan</a> in the Challenge Cup final, despite being huge underdogs. The team then hit troubled times before reforming in 2003. Since then they have played their rugby in the Championship (second tier). In 2011, they made the playoffs finishing in fifth place. They made the Grand Final, by defeating <a href="/wiki/Leigh_Centurions" title="Leigh Centurions">Leigh</a>, who were huge favourites in a playoff semi final. In the final, they were comprehensively beaten by <a href="/wiki/Featherstone_Rovers" title="Featherstone Rovers">Featherstone Rovers</a>. Sheffield also put in a bid to be a host city for the <a href="/wiki/2013_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2013 Rugby League World Cup">2013 Rugby League World Cup</a>, but their bid was unsuccessful.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:English_Institute_of_Sport_Sheffield.png" class="image"><img alt="A Modern sporting facility. The building is roughly rectangular in shape and is quite modern, with a wooden clad design. It is surrounded by greenery and has several tall, white spikes on its roof." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/English_Institute_of_Sport_Sheffield.png/220px-English_Institute_of_Sport_Sheffield.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/English_Institute_of_Sport_Sheffield.png/330px-English_Institute_of_Sport_Sheffield.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/English_Institute_of_Sport_Sheffield.png/440px-English_Institute_of_Sport_Sheffield.png 2x" data-file-width="873" data-file-height="657" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:English_Institute_of_Sport_Sheffield.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>English Institute of Sport, Sheffield</div></div></div>
<p>Sheffield is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Steelers" title="Sheffield Steelers">Sheffield Steelers</a> ice hockey team who play out of the 8,500 seater <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Arena" title="Sheffield Arena">Sheffield Arena</a>. They play in the 10 team professional <a href="/wiki/Elite_Ice_Hockey_League" title="Elite Ice Hockey League">Elite Ice Hockey League</a>. The <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Cup" title="Stanley Cup">Stanley Cup</a> was made in Sheffield in 1892. Sheffield is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Steel_Rollergirls" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield Steel Rollergirls">Sheffield Steel Rollergirls</a>, a roller derby team.
</p><p>Many of Sheffield's sporting facilities were built for the <a href="/wiki/Universiade" title="Universiade">World Student Games</a>, which the city hosted in 1991, including Sheffield Arena and the <a href="/wiki/Ponds_Forge" title="Ponds Forge">Ponds Forge</a> international diving and swimming complex. Ponds Forge is also the home of <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_City_Swimming_Club" title="Sheffield City Swimming Club">Sheffield City Swimming Club</a>, a local swimming club competing in the <a href="/wiki/Speedo" title="Speedo">Speedo</a> league. The former <a href="/wiki/Don_Valley_Stadium" title="Don Valley Stadium">Don Valley International Athletics Stadium</a>, once the largest athletics stadium in the UK, was also constructed for the Universiade games.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Ski_Village" title="Sheffield Ski Village">Sheffield Ski Village</a> was the largest artificial <a href="/wiki/Ski" title="Ski">ski</a> resort in Europe, before being destroyed in a series of suspected arson attacks in 2012 and 2013. The city also has two indoor climbing centres. Sheffield was the UK's first National City of Sport and is now home to the <a href="/wiki/English_Institute_of_Sport_%E2%80%93_Sheffield" class="mw-redirect" title="English Institute of Sport – Sheffield">English Institute of Sport – Sheffield</a>, where British athletes trained for the 2012 Olympics.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sheffield also has close ties with <a href="/wiki/Snooker" title="Snooker">snooker</a>, with the city's <a href="/wiki/Crucible_Theatre" title="Crucible Theatre">Crucible Theatre</a> being the venue for the <a href="/wiki/World_Snooker_Championship" title="World Snooker Championship">World Snooker Championships</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> The English Institute of Sport hosts most of the top fencing competitions each year, including the National Championships for Seniors, Juniors (U20's) and Cadets (U17's) as well as the 2011 Senior European Fencing Championships. The English <a href="/wiki/Squash_(sport)" title="Squash (sport)">squash</a> open is also held in the city every year. The International Open and World Matchplay Championship <a href="/wiki/Bowls" title="Bowls">bowls</a> tournaments have both been held at <a href="/wiki/Ponds_Forge" title="Ponds Forge">Ponds Forge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> The city also hosts the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Tigers_RUFC" title="Sheffield Tigers RUFC">Sheffield Tigers</a> <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Sharks" title="Sheffield Sharks">Sheffield Sharks</a>, American Football team the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Giants" title="Sheffield Giants">Sheffield Giants</a>, basketball, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_University_Bankers_Hockey_Club" title="Sheffield University Bankers Hockey Club">Sheffield University Bankers</a> <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Steelers" title="Sheffield Steelers">Sheffield Steelers</a> <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Tigers_(Speedway)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield Tigers (Speedway)">Sheffield Tigers</a> <a href="/wiki/Motorcycle_speedway" title="Motorcycle speedway">speedway</a> teams. Sheffield also has many golf courses all around the city.
</p><p>Sheffield was selected as a candidate host city by the <a href="/wiki/The_FA" class="mw-redirect" title="The FA">Football Association (FA)</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/English_2018_and_2022_FIFA_World_Cup_bid" class="mw-redirect" title="English 2018 and 2022 FIFA World Cup bid">English 2018 and 2022 FIFA World Cup bid</a> on 16 December 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Hillsborough_Stadium" title="Hillsborough Stadium">Hillsborough Stadium</a> was chosen as the proposed venue for matches in Sheffield.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> The bid failed.
</p><p>Sheffield hosted the finish of Stage 2 of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Tour_de_France" title="2014 Tour de France">2014 Tour de France</a>. Within the City limits and located just 4 kilometres (2.5&#160;mi) from the finish, was the ninth and final climb of the stage, the Category 4 Côte de Jenkin Road. The one point in the <a href="/wiki/King_of_the_Mountains" title="King of the Mountains">King of the Mountains</a> competition was claimed by <a href="/wiki/Chris_Froome" title="Chris Froome">Chris Froome</a> of <a href="/wiki/Team_Sky" class="mw-redirect" title="Team Sky">Team Sky</a>. The climb was just 0.8 kilometres (0.50&#160;mi) long at an average gradient of 10.8%. The stage was won by the eventual overall winner, <a href="/wiki/Vincenzo_Nibali" title="Vincenzo Nibali">Vincenzo Nibali</a> of <a href="/wiki/Astana_Pro_Team" title="Astana Pro Team">Astana Pro Team</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_attractions">Culture and attractions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Culture and attractions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Sheffield" title="Culture of Sheffield">Culture of Sheffield</a></div>
<p>Sheffield made the shortlist for the first city to be designated <a href="/wiki/UK_City_of_Culture" title="UK City of Culture">UK City of Culture</a>, but in July 2010 it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Derry" title="Derry">Derry</a> had been selected.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Attractions">Attractions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Attractions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Visitor_attractions_in_Sheffield" class="mw-redirect" title="Visitor attractions in Sheffield">Visitor attractions in Sheffield</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bishops_House_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Bishops_House_2011.jpg/220px-Bishops_House_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Bishops_House_2011.jpg/330px-Bishops_House_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Bishops_House_2011.jpg/440px-Bishops_House_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bishops_House_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bishops' House</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mappin_Art_Gallery_Sheffield.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Mappin_Art_Gallery_Sheffield.jpg/220px-Mappin_Art_Gallery_Sheffield.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Mappin_Art_Gallery_Sheffield.jpg/330px-Mappin_Art_Gallery_Sheffield.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Mappin_Art_Gallery_Sheffield.jpg/440px-Mappin_Art_Gallery_Sheffield.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1157" data-file-height="743" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mappin_Art_Gallery_Sheffield.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Grade_II*_listed" class="mw-redirect" title="Grade II* listed">Grade II* listed</a> <a href="/wiki/Weston_Park_Museum" title="Weston Park Museum">Weston Park Museum</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Legends" title="Sheffield Legends">Sheffield Walk of Fame</a> in the City Centre honours famous Sheffield residents past and present in a similar way to the Hollywood version.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> Sheffield also had its own Ferris Wheel known as the <a href="/wiki/Wheel_of_Sheffield" title="Wheel of Sheffield">Wheel of Sheffield</a>, located atop Fargate shopping precinct. The Wheel was dismantled in October 2010 and moved to London's Hyde Park.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Heeley City Farm and <a href="/wiki/Graves_Park" title="Graves Park">Graves Park</a> are home to Sheffield's two farm animal collections, both of which are fully open to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Sheffield also has its own zoo; the Tropical Butterfly House, Wildlife &amp; Falconry Centre.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are about <a href="/wiki/Listed_buildings_in_Sheffield" title="Listed buildings in Sheffield">1,100&#160;listed buildings in Sheffield</a> (including the whole of the <a href="/wiki/S_postcode_area" title="S postcode area">Sheffield postal district</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Of these, only five are Grade I listed. Sixty-seven are Grade II*, but the overwhelming majority are listed as Grade II.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Compared to other English cities, Sheffield has few buildings with the highest Grade I listing: <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>, for example, has <a href="/wiki/Listed_buildings_in_Liverpool" title="Listed buildings in Liverpool">26 Grade I</a> <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">listed buildings</a>. This situation led the noted architecture historian <a href="/wiki/Nikolaus_Pevsner" title="Nikolaus Pevsner">Nikolaus Pevsner</a>, writing in 1959, to comment that the city was "architecturally a miserable disappointment", with no pre-19th-century buildings of any distinction.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> By contrast, in November 2007, Sheffield's Peace and Winter Gardens beat London's South Bank to gain the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Institute_of_British_Architects" title="Royal Institute of British Architects">Royal Institute of British Architects</a>' Academy of Urbanism "Great Place" Award, as an "outstanding example of how cities can be improved, to make urban spaces as attractive and accessible as possible".<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>  In the summer of 2016 a public art event across the city occurred called the <a href="/wiki/Herd_of_Sheffield" title="Herd of Sheffield">Herd of Sheffield</a> which raised £410,000 for the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Children%27s_Hospital" title="Sheffield Children&#39;s Hospital">Sheffield Children's Hospital</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-herd_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-herd-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_musicians_from_Sheffield" title="List of musicians from Sheffield">List of musicians from Sheffield</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Sheffield_Arena.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/The_Sheffield_Arena.jpg/220px-The_Sheffield_Arena.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/The_Sheffield_Arena.jpg/330px-The_Sheffield_Arena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/The_Sheffield_Arena.jpg/440px-The_Sheffield_Arena.jpg 2x" data-file-width="572" data-file-height="369" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Sheffield_Arena.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sheffield Arena</div></div></div>
<p>Sheffield has been home to several well-known bands and musicians, with a notably large number of <a href="/wiki/Synthpop" class="mw-redirect" title="Synthpop">synthpop</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic</a> bands originating from the city.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> These include <a href="/wiki/The_Human_League" title="The Human League">The Human League</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heaven_17" title="Heaven 17">Heaven 17</a>, <a href="/wiki/ABC_(band)" title="ABC (band)">ABC</a> and the more <a href="/wiki/Industrial_music" title="Industrial music">industrially</a> inclined <a href="/wiki/Cabaret_Voltaire_(band)" title="Cabaret Voltaire (band)">Cabaret Voltaire</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Clock_DVA" title="Clock DVA">Clock DVA</a>. This electronic tradition has continued: <a href="/wiki/Techno_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Techno music">techno</a> label <a href="/wiki/Warp_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Warp Records">Warp Records</a> was a central pillar of the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Bleeps_and_Bass" class="mw-redirect" title="Yorkshire Bleeps and Bass">Yorkshire Bleeps and Bass</a> scene of the early 1990s, and has gone on to become one of the UK's oldest and best-loved dance music labels. More recently, other popular genres of electronic music such as <a href="/wiki/Bassline_house" class="mw-redirect" title="Bassline house">bassline house</a> have originated in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Sheffield was once home to a number of historically important nightclubs in the early dance music scene of the 1980s and 1990s, <a href="/wiki/Gatecrasher" title="Gatecrasher">Gatecrasher One</a> was one of the most popular clubs in the North of England until its destruction by fire on 18 June 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A number of major music acts, including <a href="/wiki/Joe_Cocker" title="Joe Cocker">Joe Cocker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Def_Leppard" title="Def Leppard">Def Leppard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Monkeys" title="Arctic Monkeys">Arctic Monkeys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bring_Me_the_Horizon" title="Bring Me the Horizon">Bring Me the Horizon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rolo_Tomassi" title="Rolo Tomassi">Rolo Tomassi</a>, <a href="/wiki/While_She_Sleeps" title="While She Sleeps">While She Sleeps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pulp_(band)" title="Pulp (band)">Pulp</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moloko" title="Moloko">Moloko</a>, hail from the city.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Indie_(music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Indie (music)">Indie</a> band <a href="/wiki/The_Long_Blondes" title="The Long Blondes">The Long Blondes</a> originated from the city,<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> as part of what the <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> dubbed the <a href="/wiki/New_Yorkshire" title="New Yorkshire">New Yorkshire</a> scene.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_city_hall_2.png" class="image"><img alt="Sheffield City Hall, a Neo-classical design with a large portico and prominent pillars which were damaged when a bomb fell on the adjoining Barkers Pool during the Second World War. It is a grade II* listed building" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Sheffield_city_hall_2.png/220px-Sheffield_city_hall_2.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Sheffield_city_hall_2.png/330px-Sheffield_city_hall_2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Sheffield_city_hall_2.png/440px-Sheffield_city_hall_2.png 2x" data-file-width="874" data-file-height="657" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_city_hall_2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sheffield City Hall, a Grade II* listed building</div></div></div>
<p>In 1999 the <a href="/wiki/National_Centre_for_Popular_Music" title="National Centre for Popular Music">National Centre for Popular Music</a>, a museum dedicated to the subject of <a href="/wiki/Popular_music" title="Popular music">popular music</a>, was opened in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> It was not as successful as was hoped, however, and later evolved to become a live music venue; then in February 2005, the unusual steel-covered building became the <a href="/wiki/Students%27_union" title="Students&#39; union">students' union</a> for <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Hallam_University" title="Sheffield Hallam University">Sheffield Hallam University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Live music venues in the city include the Harley Hotel, <a href="/wiki/Leadmill" class="mw-redirect" title="Leadmill">Leadmill</a>, West Street Live, the <a href="/wiki/Boardwalk_(nightclub)" title="Boardwalk (nightclub)">Boardwalk</a>, Dove &amp; Rainbow, The Greystones, The Casbah, <a href="/wiki/The_Cremorne,_Sheffield" class="mw-redirect" title="The Cremorne, Sheffield">The Cremorne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corporation_(nightclub)" title="Corporation (nightclub)">Corporation</a>, New Barrack Tavern, The Broadfield Hotel, Redstone bar and nightclub, the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_City_Hall" title="Sheffield City Hall">City Hall</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sheffield_Students%27_Union" title="University of Sheffield Students&#39; Union">University of Sheffield Students' Union</a>, the Studio Theatre at the <a href="/wiki/Crucible_Theatre" title="Crucible Theatre">Crucible Theatre</a>, the <a href="/wiki/O2_Academy_Sheffield" title="O2 Academy Sheffield">O2 Academy Sheffield</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Grapes,_Sheffield" class="mw-redirect" title="The Grapes, Sheffield">The Grapes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sheffield hosts a number of festivals, the Grin Up North Sheffield Comedy Festival,<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Sensoria_Music_%26_Film_Festival" title="Sensoria Music &amp; Film Festival">Sensoria Music &amp; Film Festival</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tramlines_Festival" title="Tramlines Festival">Tramlines Festival</a>. The Tramlines Festival was launched as an annual music festival in 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> it is held throughout venues in <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_City_Centre" title="Sheffield City Centre">Sheffield City Centre</a>, and features local and national artists.<sup id="cite_ref-tramlines_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tramlines-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The city is home to several local orchestras and choirs, such as the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Sheffield Symphony Orchestra">Sheffield Symphony Orchestra</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="Sheffield Philharmonic Orchestra">Sheffield Philharmonic Orchestra</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Chamber_Orchestra" title="Sheffield Chamber Orchestra">Sheffield Chamber Orchestra</a>, the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Sheffield_Youth_Orchestra" title="City of Sheffield Youth Orchestra">City of Sheffield Youth Orchestra</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Philharmonic_Chorus" title="Sheffield Philharmonic Chorus">Sheffield Philharmonic Chorus</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chorus_UK" title="Chorus UK">Chorus UK</a> community choir.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> It is also home to <a href="/wiki/Music_in_the_Round" title="Music in the Round">Music in the Round</a>, a charitable organisation that exists to promote chamber music. It describes itself as the largest promoter of chamber music outside London.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatres">Theatres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Theatres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Crucible_theatre.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Sheffield_Crucible_theatre.png/220px-Sheffield_Crucible_theatre.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Sheffield_Crucible_theatre.png/330px-Sheffield_Crucible_theatre.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Sheffield_Crucible_theatre.png/440px-Sheffield_Crucible_theatre.png 2x" data-file-width="873" data-file-height="656" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Crucible_theatre.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Crucible_Theatre" title="Crucible Theatre">Crucible Theatre</a> (centre) and Lyceum Theatre (right)</div></div></div>
<p>Sheffield has two large theatres, the <a href="/wiki/Lyceum_Theatre_(Sheffield)" title="Lyceum Theatre (Sheffield)">Lyceum Theatre</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Crucible_Theatre" title="Crucible Theatre">Crucible Theatre</a>, which together with the smaller <a href="/wiki/Studio_Theatre_(Sheffield)" title="Studio Theatre (Sheffield)">Studio Theatre</a> make up the largest theatre complex outside London, located in <a href="/wiki/Tudor_Square" title="Tudor Square">Tudor Square</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> The Crucible Theatre is the home (since 1977) of the <a href="/wiki/World_Snooker_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="World Snooker Championships">World Snooker Championships</a> and hosts many well-known stage productions throughout the year. The Lyceum, which opened in 1897, serves as a venue for touring <a href="/wiki/West_End_theatre" title="West End theatre">West End productions</a> and operas by <a href="/wiki/Opera_North" title="Opera North">Opera North</a>, as well as locally produced shows. Sheffield also has the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Montgomery_Theatre&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Montgomery Theatre (page does not exist)">Montgomery Theatre</a>, a small 420 seater theatre located a short distance from Tudor Square, opposite the town hall on Surrey Street.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> There are also a large number of smaller amateur theatres scattered throughout the city.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sheffield's museums are managed by two distinct organisations. <a href="/wiki/Museums_Sheffield" class="mw-redirect" title="Museums Sheffield">Museums Sheffield</a> manages the <a href="/wiki/Weston_Park_Museum" title="Weston Park Museum">Weston Park Museum</a> (a Grade II* listed Building), <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Galleries" class="mw-redirect" title="Millennium Galleries">Millennium Galleries</a> and <a href="/wiki/Graves_Art_Gallery" title="Graves Art Gallery">Graves Art Gallery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Industrial_Museums_Trust" title="Sheffield Industrial Museums Trust">Sheffield Industrial Museums Trust</a> manages the museums dedicated to Sheffield's industrial heritage of which there are three.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kelham_Island_Museum" title="Kelham Island Museum">Kelham Island Museum</a> (located just to the North of the city centre) showcases the city's history of steel manufacturing.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Abbeydale_Industrial_Hamlet" title="Abbeydale Industrial Hamlet">Abbeydale Industrial Hamlet</a> (in the south of the city) is a Grade I Listed building and a <a href="/wiki/Scheduled_Ancient_Monument" class="mw-redirect" title="Scheduled Ancient Monument">Scheduled Ancient Monument</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Shepherd_Wheel" title="Shepherd Wheel">Shepherd Wheel</a> (in the south-East of the city) is a former water-powered grinding <a href="/wiki/Workshop" title="Workshop">workshop</a>, Grade II listed and a Scheduled Ancient Monument.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> Also there are <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Archives" title="Sheffield Archives">Sheffield Archives</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greenspace">Greenspace</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Greenspace">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Winter_Gardens_%26_St._Paul%27s_Tower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Sheffield_Winter_Gardens_%26_St._Paul%27s_Tower.jpg/220px-Sheffield_Winter_Gardens_%26_St._Paul%27s_Tower.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Sheffield_Winter_Gardens_%26_St._Paul%27s_Tower.jpg/330px-Sheffield_Winter_Gardens_%26_St._Paul%27s_Tower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Sheffield_Winter_Gardens_%26_St._Paul%27s_Tower.jpg/440px-Sheffield_Winter_Gardens_%26_St._Paul%27s_Tower.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4033" data-file-height="2670" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Winter_Gardens_%26_St._Paul%27s_Tower.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sheffield Winter Gardens &amp; St Paul's Tower</div></div></div>
<p>Sheffield has a reputed 4.5 million trees<sup id="cite_ref-GEO_treecount_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GEO_treecount-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and has been described as the greenest city in Europe,<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> despite a large number of highway tree fellings taking place across the city since 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> There are many parks and woods throughout the city and beyond. Containing more than 250 parks, woodlands and gardens, there are around 78 public parks and 10 public gardens in Sheffield,<sup id="cite_ref-sheffgeog_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheffgeog-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> including 83 managed parks (13 'City' Parks, 20 'District' Parks and 50 'Local' Parks) located throughout the city.<sup id="cite_ref-About_the_Parks_&amp;_Countryside_Service_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_the_Parks_&amp;_Countryside_Service-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> Included in the city parks category are 3 of Sheffield's 6 public gardens (the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Botanical_Gardens" title="Sheffield Botanical Gardens">Sheffield Botanical Gardens</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Peace_Gardens" title="Peace Gardens">Peace Gardens</a> and Hillsborough Walled Gardens, with the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Winter_Gardens" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield Winter Gardens">Sheffield Winter Gardens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beauchief_Gardens" title="Beauchief Gardens">Beauchief Gardens</a> and Lynwood Gardens being the separate entities).
</p><p>The Sheffield Botanical Gardens are on a 19-acre site located to the south west of the city centre and date back to 1836. The site includes a large, Grade II listed, Victorian era <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse" title="Greenhouse">glasshouse</a>. The Peace Gardens, neighboured next to the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Town_Hall" title="Sheffield Town Hall">Town Hall</a> and forming part of the Heart of the City project, occupy a 0.67 hectares (1.7 acres) site in the centre of the city. The site is dominated by its water features, principal among which is the Goodwin Fountain. Made up of 89 individual jets of water, this fountain lies at the corner of the quarter-circle shaped Peace Gardens and is named after <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Goodwin" title="Stuart Goodwin">Stuart Goodwin</a>, a notable Sheffield industrialist. Since their redevelopment in 1998, the Peace gardens have received a number of regional and national accolades.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> Hillsborough Walled Garden is located in <a href="/wiki/Hillsborough_Park" title="Hillsborough Park">Hillsborough Park</a>, to the north-west of the city centre.
