The gardens date back to 1779 and have been dedicated to the victims of the <a href="/wiki/Hillsborough_Disaster" class="mw-redirect" title="Hillsborough Disaster">Hillsborough Disaster</a> since the redevelopment of the gardens in the early 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Winter_Garden" title="Sheffield Winter Garden">The Winter Garden</a>, lying within the <a href="/wiki/Heart_of_the_City_(development)" class="mw-redirect" title="Heart of the City (development)">Heart of the City</a>, is a large wood framed, glass skinned <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse" title="Greenhouse">greenhouse</a> housing some 2,500 plants from around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Winter_Garden_-_inside.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Sheffield_Winter_Garden_-_inside.jpg/220px-Sheffield_Winter_Garden_-_inside.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Sheffield_Winter_Garden_-_inside.jpg/330px-Sheffield_Winter_Garden_-_inside.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Sheffield_Winter_Garden_-_inside.jpg/440px-Sheffield_Winter_Garden_-_inside.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1692" data-file-height="1269" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Winter_Garden_-_inside.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sheffield Winter Garden – inside 2013</div></div></div>
<p>Also within the city there are a number of <a href="/wiki/Nature_reserves" class="mw-redirect" title="Nature reserves">nature reserves</a> which when combined occupy 1,600 acres (6.5&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) of land.<sup id="cite_ref-sheffield1_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheffield1-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> There are also 170 <a href="/wiki/Woodland" title="Woodland">woodland</a> areas within the city, 80 of which are classed as ancient.<sup id="cite_ref-sheffield1_195-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheffield1-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The South West boundary of the city overlaps with the <a href="/wiki/Peak_District" title="Peak District">Peak District National Park</a>, the first national park in England (est. 1951).<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> As a consequence, several communities actually reside within both entities. The Peak District is home to many notable, natural, features and also man-made features such as <a href="/wiki/Chatsworth_House" title="Chatsworth House">Chatsworth House</a>, the setting for the BBC series <i><a href="/wiki/Pride_and_Prejudice" title="Pride and Prejudice">Pride and Prejudice</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sheffield_City_Council" title="Sheffield City Council">Sheffield City Council</a> has created a new chain of parks spanning the hillside behind <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield Station">Sheffield Station</a>. The park, known as Sheaf Valley Park, has an open-air amphitheatre and will include an arboretum.<sup id="cite_ref-sheffieldtelegraph.co.uk_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheffieldtelegraph.co.uk-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> The site was once home to a medieval deer park, latterly owned by the <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Heritage_Park" title="Norfolk Heritage Park">Duke of Norfolk</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sheffieldtelegraph.co.uk_198-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheffieldtelegraph.co.uk-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Entertainment">Entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Meadowhall_Shopping_Centre_-_The_Oasis_07-04.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Meadowhall_Shopping_Centre_-_The_Oasis_07-04.jpg/220px-Meadowhall_Shopping_Centre_-_The_Oasis_07-04.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Meadowhall_Shopping_Centre_-_The_Oasis_07-04.jpg/330px-Meadowhall_Shopping_Centre_-_The_Oasis_07-04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Meadowhall_Shopping_Centre_-_The_Oasis_07-04.jpg/440px-Meadowhall_Shopping_Centre_-_The_Oasis_07-04.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Meadowhall_Shopping_Centre_-_The_Oasis_07-04.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Oasis food court at <a href="/wiki/Meadowhall_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Meadowhall Centre">Meadowhall Centre</a></div></div></div>
<p>Sheffield has six cinema complexes, four of which are in the city centre and a further two in the Lower Don Valley. One of these complexes is located at <a href="/wiki/Valley_Centertainment" title="Valley Centertainment">Valley Centertainment</a>, a leisure and entertainment complex in the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Don_Valley" title="Lower Don Valley">Don Valley</a>. It was built on land previously occupied by <a href="/wiki/Steel_mills" class="mw-redirect" title="Steel mills">steel mills</a> near what is now Meadowhall and the Sheffield Arena. It is home to several restaurants, bars, a <a href="/wiki/Cineworld" title="Cineworld">cinema</a> <a href="/wiki/Megaplex" class="mw-redirect" title="Megaplex">multiplex</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Bowling" title="Bowling">bowling alley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> It is also the largest <a href="/wiki/Cineworld" title="Cineworld">Cineworld</a> complex in the United Kingdom, containing 20 screens in one building.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Odeon_Sheffield" title="Odeon Sheffield">Odeon Sheffield</a>, situated on Arundel Gate in the city Centre and <a href="/wiki/Vue_(cinema)" class="mw-redirect" title="Vue (cinema)">Vue</a>, located within Meadowhall Shopping Centre, are the two other mainstream cinemas in the city. The <a href="/wiki/Showroom_Cinema,_Sheffield" title="Showroom Cinema, Sheffield">Showroom</a>, an independent cinema showing non-mainstream productions, is located in <a href="/wiki/Sheaf_Square" title="Sheaf Square">Sheaf Square</a>, close to <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_station" title="Sheffield station">Sheffield station</a>. In 2002 the Showroom was voted as the best Independent cinema in the country by <i>Guardian</i> readers.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>  A <a href="/wiki/Curzon_Cinemas" title="Curzon Cinemas">Curzon Cinemas</a> complex is based in the former Sheffield Banking Company building, located just off Arundel Gate. The cinema features <a href="/wiki/4K_resolution" title="4K resolution">4K resolution</a> projectors and was opened in January 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> Sheffield's newest cinema, The Light (Sheffield), opened just off The Moor in 2018.
</p><p>Sheffield has a thriving poetry and spoken word scene: from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://opusindependents.com/wordlife/">Wordlife's</a> events across the city to the sustained work of <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.sheffieldauthors.co.uk">Sheffield Authors</a>; from the vibrant monthly arts night, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://versematters.wordpress.com">Verse Matters</a>, at the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://versematters.wordpress.com">Moor Theatre Deli</a> to the longstanding work of <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.poetrybusiness.co.uk">The Poetry Business</a>, there's always opportunities for new and experienced writers to get writing and to share their work.
</p><p>Owing to its long history, Sheffield has a large number of <a href="/wiki/Pubs" class="mw-redirect" title="Pubs">pubs</a> throughout the city. West Street, running through the heart of the <a href="/wiki/West_End,_Sheffield" title="West End, Sheffield">West End</a> district of the city centre, is home to many pubs, bars and clubs and attracts many student visitors. A recent addition to the city's nightlife is <a href="/wiki/Leopold_Square" title="Leopold Square">Leopold Square</a>, situated just off the northern end of West Street. Aagrah, an Indian restaurant in the square which serves <a href="/wiki/Kashmiri_cuisine" title="Kashmiri cuisine">Kashmiri cuisine</a>, has recently been voted "Best Restaurant Group in the UK" at the prestigious <a href="/wiki/British_Curry_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="British Curry Awards">British Curry Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_film">Media and film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Media and film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sheffield has two commercial newspapers, <i><a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Star" title="Sheffield Star">The Star</a></i>  and <i><a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Telegraph" title="Sheffield Telegraph">Sheffield Telegraph</a></i>, both published by <a href="/wiki/Johnston_Press" title="Johnston Press">Johnston Press PLC</a>. <i>The Star</i> has been published daily since 1897; the <i>Sheffield Telegraph</i>, now a weekly publication, originated in 1855.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sheffield has its own TV station; <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Live!" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield Live!">Sheffield Live TV</a>, a not-for-profit company which began broadcasting on 23 September 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> SLTV has been awarded a 12-year licence to provide the digital terrestrial broadcasting service.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Regional broadcasters <a href="/wiki/BBC_Yorkshire" title="BBC Yorkshire">BBC Yorkshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Yorkshire Television">Yorkshire Television</a> also cover the city. Five local radio stations broadcast in the city. The professional services are <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Sheffield" title="BBC Radio Sheffield">BBC Radio Sheffield</a>, the independent <a href="/wiki/Hallam_FM" title="Hallam FM">Hallam FM</a> and its sister station <a href="/wiki/Magic_AM" class="mw-redirect" title="Magic AM">Magic AM</a>. Sheffield is also home to two <a href="/wiki/FM_broadcasting" title="FM broadcasting">FM</a> licensed <a href="/wiki/Community_radio" title="Community radio">community radio</a> stations: Sheffield Live 93.2, and <a href="/wiki/Burngreave_Community_Radio" title="Burngreave Community Radio">Burngreave Community Radio</a> on 103.1.
</p><p>Sheffield Hospital Radio (Hospital Broadcasting Sheffield) broadcasts a 24-hour service to the Royal Hallamshire, Jessop Wing, Northern General and Weston Park Hospital and also offers a dedicated patient visiting service. The charity is operated by volunteers from studios at the Royal Hallamshire Hospital and is provided free to bedside terminals via Hospedia and on medium wave 1431am from a transmitter at the Northern General Hospital.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The films and plays <i><a href="/wiki/The_Full_Monty" title="The Full Monty">The Full Monty</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Threads" title="Threads">Threads</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Looks_and_Smiles_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Looks and Smiles (film)">Looks and Smiles</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/When_Saturday_Comes_(film)" title="When Saturday Comes (film)">When Saturday Comes</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Whatever_Happened_to_Harold_Smith%3F" title="Whatever Happened to Harold Smith?">Whatever Happened to Harold Smith?</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_History_Boys" title="The History Boys">The History Boys</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Four_Lions" title="Four Lions">Four Lions</a></i> are set in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/F.I.S.T." title="F.I.S.T.">F.I.S.T.</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Kill_List" title="Kill List">Kill List</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/%2771_(film)" title="&#39;71 (film)">'71</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Princess_Bride_(film)" title="The Princess Bride (film)">The Princess Bride</a></i> also include several scenes filmed in Sheffield and a substantial part of <i><a href="/wiki/Among_Giants" title="Among Giants">Among Giants</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> was filmed in the city. The documentary festival <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Doc/Fest" title="Sheffield Doc/Fest">Sheffield Doc/Fest</a> has been run annually since 1994 at the <a href="/wiki/Showroom_Cinema" class="mw-redirect" title="Showroom Cinema">Showroom Cinema</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> and in 2007 Sheffield hosted the <a href="/wiki/Awards_of_the_International_Indian_Film_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="Awards of the International Indian Film Academy">Awards of the International Indian Film Academy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> The 2018 series of <i><a href="/wiki/Doctor_Who" title="Doctor Who">Doctor Who</a></i>, which features the <a href="/wiki/Park_Hill,_Sheffield" title="Park Hill, Sheffield">Park Hill</a> estate and other Sheffield locations, premiered in Sheffield.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Folk_culture">Folk culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Folk culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sheffield has a thriving folk music, song and dance community. Singing and music sessions occur weekly in many pubs around the city and it also hosts the annual Sheffield Sessions Festival.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sheffield" title="University of Sheffield">University of Sheffield</a> runs a number of courses and research projects dedicated to folk culture.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The tradition of singing carols in pubs around Christmas is still kept alive in the city. The Sheffield Carols, as they are known locally, predate modern carols by over a century and are sung with alternative words and verses.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> Although there is a core of carols that are sung at most venues, each particular place has its own mini-tradition. The repertoire at two nearby places can vary widely, and woe betide those who try to strike up a ‘foreign’ carol. Some are unaccompanied, some have a piano or organ, there is a flip chart with the words on in one place, a string quartet (quintet, sextet, septet) accompanies the singing at another, some encourage soloists, others stick to audience participation, a brass band plays at certain events, the choir takes the lead at another.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> It is thought this tradition is now unique in Britain.
</p><p>The city is home to thirteen <a href="/wiki/Morris_dance" title="Morris dance">morris dance</a> teams – thought to be one of the highest concentration of sides in the country. Nearly all forms of the dance are represented in the city, including <a href="/wiki/Cotswold_morris" class="mw-redirect" title="Cotswold morris">Cotswold</a> (Five Rivers Morris,<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> Pecsaetan Morris,<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> Harthill Morris,<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> Lord Conyer's Morris Men,<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> Sheffield City Morris,<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> William Morris<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup>), <a href="/wiki/Border_Morris" title="Border Morris">border</a> (Boggart's Breakfast<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>), <a href="/wiki/North_West_morris" class="mw-redirect" title="North West morris">North West</a> (Yorkshire Chandelier,<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> Silkstone Greens,<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> Lizzie Dripping<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>), <a href="/wiki/Rapper_dance" class="mw-redirect" title="Rapper dance">rapper</a> (Sheffield Steel Rapper<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>) and <a href="/wiki/Long_Sword_dance" title="Long Sword dance">Yorkshire Longsword</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_services">Public services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Public services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Hallamshire_Hospital.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Royal_Hallamshire_Hospital.jpg/220px-Royal_Hallamshire_Hospital.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Royal_Hallamshire_Hospital.jpg/330px-Royal_Hallamshire_Hospital.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Royal_Hallamshire_Hospital.jpg/440px-Royal_Hallamshire_Hospital.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Hallamshire_Hospital.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Hallamshire_Hospital" title="Royal Hallamshire Hospital">Royal Hallamshire Hospital</a></div></div></div>
<p>Sheffield is policed by <a href="/wiki/South_Yorkshire_Police" title="South Yorkshire Police">South Yorkshire Police</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Territorial_police_force" title="Territorial police force">territorial police force</a>) whose headquarters are in the city. Sheffield constitutes one of its four Districts (Barnsley, Doncaster and Rotherham being the other three).<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> The force polices an area of approximately 1,554 square kilometres and is the 13th largest force in <a href="/wiki/Police_forces_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Police forces in the United Kingdom">England, Wales and Northern Ireland</a>.
</p><p>Medical services in Sheffield are provided by three NHS Foundation Trusts. <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Teaching_Hospitals_NHS_Foundation_Trust" title="Sheffield Teaching Hospitals NHS Foundation Trust">Sheffield Teaching Hospitals NHS Foundation Trust</a> provides healthcare to people (primarily adults) throughout Sheffield and South Yorkshire. The trusts title includes the word 'teaching' because it undertakes training of medical students at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sheffield" title="University of Sheffield">University of Sheffield</a> and has strong links to <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Hallam_University" title="Sheffield Hallam University">Sheffield Hallam University</a> as well. The trust has two campuses: The West Campus containing the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Hallamshire_Hospital" title="Royal Hallamshire Hospital">Royal Hallamshire Hospital</a>, the Jessop Wing (maternity wing), <a href="/wiki/Weston_Park_Hospital" title="Weston Park Hospital">Weston Park Hospital</a> (specialist cancer treatment) and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Clifford_Dental_Hospital" title="Charles Clifford Dental Hospital">Charles Clifford Dental Hospital</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Northern_General_Hospital" title="Northern General Hospital">Northern General Hospital</a> is the second 'campus' and is a large facility in the northern suburbs of Sheffield, containing the city's A&amp;E department.
<a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Children%27s_NHS_Foundation_Trust" title="Sheffield Children&#39;s NHS Foundation Trust">Sheffield Children's NHS Foundation Trust</a> provides healthcare for children within the city of Sheffield, South Yorkshire and the UK as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sheffield Health and Social Care NHS Foundation Trust provides mental health services, services for people with learning disabilities, substance misuse services, long term neurological conditions, as well as a consortium of GP practises.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>  The Sheffield Institute for Motor Neurone Disease (also known as Sheffield Institute for Translational Neuroscience – SITraN) has been developed by the University of Sheffield.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ambulances are provided by the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Ambulance_Service" title="Yorkshire Ambulance Service">Yorkshire Ambulance Service</a>, which itself is an NHS trust.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> Fire services in Sheffield are provided by <a href="/wiki/South_Yorkshire_Fire_and_Rescue_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="South Yorkshire Fire and Rescue Service">South Yorkshire Fire and Rescue Service</a>. For the purposes of fire-fighting and rescue, Sheffield is divided into East and West sub-divisions.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Domestic waste services in Sheffield are provided by <a href="/wiki/Veolia#Veolia_Environmental_Services" title="Veolia">Veolia Environmental Services</a> under contract from and on behalf of the council. Council owned/run buildings are maintained by <a href="/wiki/Kier_Group" title="Kier Group">Kier Group Sheffield</a> in partnership with the council.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sister_cities">Sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheffield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The 'Sheffield International Linking Committee' promotes Sheffield overseas, especially with five <a href="/wiki/Town_twinning" class="mw-redirect" title="Town twinning">sister cities</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/China" title="China"><img alt="China" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Chengdu" title="Chengdu">Chengdu</a>, China</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/China" title="China"><img alt="China" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Anshan" title="Anshan">Anshan</a>, China</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany"><img alt="Germany" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/35px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Bochum" title="Bochum">Bochum</a>, Germany</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine"><img alt="Ukraine" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Flag_of_Ukraine.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ukraine.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Flag_of_Ukraine.svg/35px-Flag_of_Ukraine.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Flag_of_Ukraine.svg/45px-Flag_of_Ukraine.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Donetsk" title="Donetsk">Donetsk</a>, Ukraine</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua"><img alt="Nicaragua" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Nicaragua.svg/23px-Flag_of_Nicaragua.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Nicaragua.svg/35px-Flag_of_Nicaragua.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Nicaragua.svg/46px-Flag_of_Nicaragua.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Estel%C3%AD" title="Estelí">Estelí</a>, Nicaragua</li></ul>
<p>A further four cities have a Friendship Agreement with Sheffield:
</p>
<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan"><img alt="Japan" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/45px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Kawasaki,_Kanagawa" title="Kawasaki, Kanagawa">Kawasaki</a>, Japan</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia"><img alt="Zambia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Flag_of_Zambia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Zambia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Flag_of_Zambia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Zambia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Flag_of_Zambia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Zambia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1400" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Kitwe" title="Kitwe">Kitwe</a>, Zambia</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan"><img alt="Pakistan" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Flag_of_Pakistan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Pakistan.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Flag_of_Pakistan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Pakistan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Flag_of_Pakistan.svg/45px-Flag_of_Pakistan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Kotli" title="Kotli">Kotli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azad_Kashmir" title="Azad Kashmir">Pakistan-administered Kashmir</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>, United States - This is mainly due to both cities link with the <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">Steel</a> with both cities being known as <a href="/wiki/Steel_City" title="Steel City">Steel City</a>.</li></ul>
<p>Two roads in Sheffield have been named after sister cities; a section of the A6102 in Norton is named Bochum Parkway, and a road in <a href="/wiki/Hackenthorpe" title="Hackenthorpe">Hackenthorpe</a> is named Donetsk Way. Likewise in Bochum, Germany there is a major road called the Sheffield-Ring.
</p>

<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The word <i>Wales</i> derives from the Germanic word <i><a href="/wiki/Walhaz" title="Walhaz">Walhaz</a></i>, and was originally used by the Anglo-Saxons to refer to the native Britons. In reference to the villages of Wales and Waleswood, <a href="/wiki/Sidney_Oldall_Addy" title="Sidney Oldall Addy">S.O. Addy</a>, in his <i>A Glossary of Words Used in the Neighbourhood of Sheffield</i>, p. 274, states "The Anglo-Saxon invaders or settlers called the old inhabitants or aborigines of this country wealas, or foreigners." See also, "Welsh" in <cite class="citation book">Simpson, Jacqueline; Roud, Stephen (1989). <i><a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">Oxford English Dictionary</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Clarendon_Press" class="mw-redirect" title="Clarendon Press">Clarendon Press</a>. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-19-210019-X" title="Special:BookSources/0-19-210019-X"><bdi>0-19-210019-X</bdi></a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Oxford+English+Dictionary&amp;rft.pub=Clarendon+Press&amp;rft.date=1989&amp;rft.isbn=0-19-210019-X&amp;rft.aulast=Simpson&amp;rft.aufirst=Jacqueline&amp;rft.au=Roud%2C+Stephen&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASheffield" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In an entry dated 827, the <i><a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon_Chronicle" title="Anglo-Saxon Chronicle">Anglo-Saxon Chronicle</a></i> states "Egbert led an army against the Northumbrians as far as Dore, where they met him, and offered terms of obedience and subjection, on the acceptance of which they returned home" (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://mcllibrary.org/Anglo/part2.html">transcription</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20180413124643/http://mcllibrary.org/Anglo/part2.html">Archived</a> 13 April 2018 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>). Most sources (for example Vickers, <i>Old Sheffield Town</i>) state that the date given in the chronicle is incorrect, and that 829 is the more likely date for this event.</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-number_of_hills-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-number_of_hills_41-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It is often stated that Sheffield is built on seven hills (for an example, see <a href="/wiki/George_Orwell" title="George Orwell">George Orwell</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Road_to_Wigan_Pier" title="The Road to Wigan Pier">The Road to Wigan Pier</a></i>). </li>

Cushman &amp; Wakefield. 2008.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=UK+Cities+Monitor+2008&amp;rft.pub=Cushman+%26+Wakefield&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASheffield" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-84"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-84">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">There are numerous sources showing the international reputation of Sheffield for metallurgy, and in particular steel and cutlery manufacture. Some examples are: the <a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">Oxford English Dictionary</a>, which begins its entry for <i>Sheffield</i>, "The name of a manufacturing city of Yorkshire, famous for cutlery"; and the <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclopædia Britannica">Encyclopædia Britannica</a></i>, which in its entry for "Sheffield" states that by 1830 Sheffield had earned "recognition as the world centre of high-grade steel manufacture". <a href="/wiki/David_Hey" title="David Hey">David Hey</a> in the preface to his 1997 book <i>Mesters to Masters: A History of the Company of Cutlers in Hallamshire.</i> (<a href="/wiki/Oxford_University_Press" title="Oxford University Press">Oxford University Press</a>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-19-828997-9" title="Special:BookSources/0-19-828997-9">0-19-828997-9</a>) states "It (Sheffield) was known for its cutlery wares long before the incorporation of the <a href="/wiki/Company_of_Cutlers_in_Hallamshire" title="Company of Cutlers in Hallamshire">Cutlers' Company</a> in 1624, and long before it acquired an international reputation as the steel capital of the world."</span>
</li>
